10037{_}2683{_}Mrs. Everidge caught Evadne close in a last embrace.
10037{_}2684{_}"My precious little sister, I shall miss you every day!"
10037{_}2685{_}Then she was gone, and Evadne, looking eagerly out of her window, saw the dear face, from which the tears had been swept away, smiling brightly at her from the platform.
10037{_}2686{_}"You magnificent Christian!"
10037{_}2687{_}she cried.
10037{_}2688{_}"You will give others the sunshine always!"
10037{_}2689{_}*       *       *       *       *  The train steamed into the station at Marlborough and again Louis came forward to greet her with a look of admiration on his unusually animated face.
10037{_}2690{_}"Well done, Evadne!
10037{_}2691{_}If the atmosphere of Vernon can work such transformation as this, it ought to be bottled up and sold at twenty dollars the dozen.
10037{_}2692{_}You go away looking like a snow-wraith, and you return a blooming Hebe."
10037{_}2693{_}Evadne laughed merrily.
10037{_}2694{_}"Thank you.
10037{_}2695{_}The atmosphere of Vernon has a wonderful power," but it was not of the material ozone she was thinking as she spoke.
10037{_}2696{_}"I believe I will try it.
10037{_}2697{_}My constitution is running down at the rate of an alarm clock.
10037{_}2698{_}I must take my choice between a tonic and an early grave.
10037{_}2699{_}Will you vouch for like good results in my case?"
10037{_}2700{_}Evadne shook her head.
10037{_}2701{_}"I do not believe it would have the same effect upon everyone," she said.
10037{_}2702{_}"Ah, then I shall be compelled to go to Europe."
10037{_}2703{_}Evadne looked at him.
10037{_}2704{_}"Yes," she said, "I think Europe would suit you better."
10037{_}2705{_}"That is unfortunate,--for the Judge's purse.
10037{_}2706{_}How is Aunt Marthe?"
10037{_}2707{_}"She is well," she answered with a sudden stillness in her voice.
10037{_}2708{_}She could not trust herself to talk about this friend of hers to careless questioners.
10037{_}2709{_}"How is Uncle Lawrence, and all the others?"
10037{_}2710{_}"The Judge is in his usual state of health, I fancy.
10037{_}2711{_}We rarely meet except at the table and then you know personal questions are not considered in good form.
10037{_}2712{_}The others are well, and Isabelle, having just returned from the metropolis of Fashion, is more than ever _au fait_ in the usages of polite society.
10037{_}2713{_}But none of them have improved like you, little coz.
10037{_}2714{_}What has changed you so?"
10037{_}2715{_}And she answered softly, with a new light shining in her lovely eyes,--"Jesus Christ."
10037{_}2716{_}*       *       *       *       *  "You poor Evadne!"
10037{_}2717{_}said Marion that evening, "what a dreary summer you must have had, shut away among those stupid mountains!
10037{_}2718{_}If you could only have been with me, now.
10037{_}2719{_}I never had such a lovely vacation in my life.
10037{_}2720{_}There seemed to be some excitement every day;--picnics and boating parties and tennis matches and five o'clocks----"  Evadne laughed.
10037{_}2721{_}"You would better not let Uncle Horace know you are 'a votary of the deadly five o'clock' or he will empty his vials of denunciation upon your unlucky head.
10037{_}2722{_}"Oh, Aunt Kate, he sent you a large bundle of fraternal greetings.
10037{_}2723{_}He says that, 'viewed through the glamour of memory, you impress him like an Alpine landscape, when the sun is rising, and he hopes the soft brilliance of prosperity will ever envelop you in its radiance and serve to enhance the beauty of your stately calm.'"
10037{_}2724{_}Mrs. Hildreth smiled, well pleased.
10037{_}2725{_}"Horace is so poetical," she said, "but all the Everidges are clever.
10037{_}2726{_}What a shame it seems that a man of his talent should be forced by ill health to exist in a place where there is not a single soul capable of appreciating his rare qualities.
10037{_}2727{_}Even his wife does not begin to understand him.
10037{_}2728{_}It seems like casting pearls before swine."
10037{_}2729{_}Evadne's eyes flashed and her lips pressed themselves tightly together, but Mrs. Hildreth's gaze was fixed intently upon the lace shawl she was knitting and Louis just then gave a sudden turn to the conversation.
10037{_}2730{_}She went up to her room with a great homesickness surging at her heart.
10037{_}2731{_}Only last night all had been lightsome and happy, now the old darkness seemed to have settled down about her again.
10037{_}2732{_}She knelt before her window and looked at the strip of sky which was all a Marlborough residence allowed her.
10037{_}2733{_}"Happy stars!"
10037{_}2734{_}she murmured, "for you are shining on Aunt Marthe!"
10037{_}2735{_}Far into the night she knelt there, until a great peace flooded her soul.
10037{_}2736{_}She raised her hands towards the sparkling sky.
10037{_}2737{_}"To make the world brighter, to make the world better, to lift the world nearer to God.
10037{_}2738{_}Blessed Christ, that was thy mission.
10037{_}2739{_}I will make it mine!"
10037{_}2740{_}The next morning Louis drew her aside.
10037{_}2741{_}"So, little coz, you did not coincide with the lady mother's eulogium of our respected collateral last night?"
10037{_}2742{_}"Why, I said nothing!"
10037{_}2743{_}cried Evadne in astonishment.
10037{_}2744{_}Louis laughed.
10037{_}2745{_}"Have you never heard of eyes that speak and faces that tell tales?"
10037{_}2746{_}he said.
10037{_}2747{_}"I will just whisper a word of warning before you play havoc with your web of destiny.
10037{_}2748{_}Don't let a suspicion of your dislike cross the lady mother's mind, for Uncle Horace is her beau-ideal of a man.
10037{_}2749{_}I agree with you.
10037{_}2750{_}I think he is a cad."
10037{_}2751{_}CHAPTER XVI.
10037{_}2752{_}"An invitation to Professor Joliette's," and Isabelle tossed a gilt-edged card across the table to Marion; "Wednesday evening.
10037{_}2753{_}It's not a very long invitation.
10037{_}2754{_}What dress will you wear?"
10037{_}2755{_}"But you are engaged, Marion," said Evadne; "Wednesday evening, you know."
10037{_}2756{_}"Yes," said Marion with a sigh, "it is awkward.
10037{_}2757{_}I do wish they would choose some other night for prayer meeting.
10037{_}2758{_}Wednesday seems such a favorite with everybody."
10037{_}2759{_}"What a little prig you are getting to be, Evadne!"
10037{_}2760{_}said Isabelle with a sneer.
10037{_}2761{_}"Your only diversion seems to be prayer meeting and church.
10037{_}2762{_}You are as bad as Aunt Marthe."
10037{_}2763{_}"Aunt Marthe a prig!
10037{_}2764{_}Oh, that is too funny!"
10037{_}2765{_}and Evadne gave one of her low, sweet laughs.
10037{_}2766{_}"Besides, does keeping one's engagements constitute a prig, Isabelle?
10037{_}2767{_}You wouldn't think so if you were invited to the President's reception."
10037{_}2768{_}"The President's reception!
10037{_}2769{_}What does get into the child!
10037{_}2770{_}I don't see much analogy between the two cases.
10037{_}2771{_}No one considers prayer meeting a binding engagement, and I'm sure we go as often as we can."
10037{_}2772{_}"Not binding!"
10037{_}2773{_}echoed Evadne.
10037{_}2774{_}"So Christ is not of as much importance as the President of the United States!"
10037{_}2775{_}"You do have such a way of putting things, Evadne!"
10037{_}2776{_}said Marion thoughtfully.
10037{_}2777{_}"I expect we had better refuse, Isabelle."
10037{_}2778{_}"Refuse,--nonsense!"
10037{_}2779{_}said Isabelle sharply.
10037{_}2780{_}"You always meet the best people at the Joliettes',--besides, why should we run the risk of offending them?"
10037{_}2781{_}"Why should they run the risk of offending you, by choosing a night they know you cannot come?"
10037{_}2782{_}asked Evadne.
10037{_}2783{_}"Ridiculous!
10037{_}2784{_}What do they care about our church concerns?
10037{_}2785{_}The Joliettes are foreigners.
10037{_}2786{_}People in polite society do not give religion such an unpleasant prominence as you delight in, Evadne.
10037{_}2787{_}For my part, I consider it very bad form."
10037{_}2788{_}"Breakers ahead, Evadne," said Louis with his cynical laugh.
10037{_}2789{_}"Good form is Isabelle's fetich.
10037{_}2790{_}Woe betide the unlucky wight who dares to hold an opinion of his own."
10037{_}2791{_}"But," said Evadne, the old puzzled look coming into her eyes, "I wish I could understand.
10037{_}2792{_}Are Christians ashamed of the religion of Jesus?"
10037{_}2793{_}"That's about the amount of it, little coz.
10037{_}2794{_}It is a sort of kedge anchor which they keep on board in case of danger.
10037{_}2795{_}For my part I think it is better to sail clear.
10037{_}2796{_}It is only an uncomfortable addition which spoils the trim of the ship."
10037{_}2797{_}"Oh, Louis, don't!"
10037{_}2798{_}exclaimed Marion with a sigh.
10037{_}2799{_}"It is so hard to know what is right!
10037{_}2800{_}Sometimes I wish I were a nun, shut up in a convent, and then I should have nothing else to do."
10037{_}2801{_}"Doubtless the Lord would appreciate that sort of faithfulness," said Louis gravely, "although I notice Christianity seems to be a sort of Sing-Sing arrangement with the majority.
10037{_}2802{_}Everything is done under a sense of compulsion, and the air is lurid with trials and lamentations and woe.
10037{_}2803{_}It is not an alluring life, and, in my opinion, the jolly old world shows its sense in steering clear of it."
10037{_}2804{_}"Your irreverence is shocking, Louis," said Isabelle severely, "and you are as much of an extremist as Evadne.
10037{_}2805{_}No one could live such a life as you seem to expect.
10037{_}2806{_}Religion has its proper place, of course, but I do not think it is wise to speak of the deep things of life on all occasions."
10037{_}2807{_}"'I determined not to know anything among you, save Jesus Christ, and him crucified,'" quoted Evadne.
10037{_}2808{_}"Was Paul mistaken then?"
10037{_}2809{_}"Certainly, my dear coz," said Louis, as he prepared to leave the room.
10037{_}2810{_}"The greatest men are subject to that infirmity.
10037{_}2811{_}The only one who has never been mistaken is Isabelle."
10037{_}2812{_}*       *       *       *       *  "It is so provoking that we cannot have the carriage," grumbled Isabelle, as, when Wednesday evening came, they waited for Louis in the dining-room.
10037{_}2813{_}"At the Joliettes' of all places!
10037{_}2814{_}I am sure I don't see, Papa, why you cannot insist upon Pompey's taking some other night off when we need him on Wednesdays.
10037{_}2815{_}It is horribly awkward!"
10037{_}2816{_}Her father shook his head as he slowly peeled an orange.
10037{_}2817{_}"Because I have given him my word, my dear.
10037{_}2818{_}The only stipulation he made when I engaged him was that he should not be required to drive on Sundays and Wednesday evenings, and, when I hear people complaining about their surly, incapable coachmen, I consider it is a light price to pay.
10037{_}2819{_}Pompey is as sober as a church and as pleasant-tempered in a rain storm as a water-spaniel,--no matter what hour of the night you keep him waiting; so it is the least we can do to let the poor fellow be sure of one evening to himself;" and the Judge opened his Times and began to study the money market.
10037{_}2820{_}"Well," said Isabelle crossly.
10037{_}2821{_}"I, for one, don't believe in allowing servants to have such cast-iron rules.
10037{_}2822{_}It savors too much of socialism."
10037{_}2823{_}"Exactly so," said Louis from the doorway, where he stood leisurely buttoning his gloves.
10037{_}2824{_}"You will never pose as the goddess of liberty, _ma belle soeur_.
10037{_}2825{_}It is a good thing that Lincoln got the Emancipation bill signed before you came into power, or dusky millions might still be weeping tears of blood."
10037{_}2826{_}Isabelle swept past him with an indignant toss of her head, and the front door closed after the trio with a metallic clang.
10037{_}2827{_}"I don't wonder the poor child is annoyed," said Mrs. Hildreth as she played with her grapes.
10037{_}2828{_}"It is very embarrassing when people know that we keep a carriage; and the Joliettes are such sticklers in the matter of etiquette.
10037{_}2829{_}It is a ridiculous fad of yours, Lawrence, to be so punctilious."
10037{_}2830{_}"But, my dear, I gave him my word of honor!"
10037{_}2831{_}"What if you did?
10037{_}2832{_}There are exceptions to every rule."
10037{_}2833{_}"Not in the Hildreth code of honor, Kate."
10037{_}2834{_}"Nonsense!
10037{_}2835{_}What does a colored coachman understand about that!
10037{_}2836{_}Why, Evadne, you cannot go to prayer meeting alone!"
10037{_}2837{_}she exclaimed, as Evadne came into the room with her hat on.
10037{_}2838{_}"Your uncle is busy and I am too tired, so there is no way for you to get home."
10037{_}2839{_}"I am going to Dyce's church, Aunt Kate.
10037{_}2840{_}Pompey will bring me home."
10037{_}2841{_}"Among a lot of shouting negroes!
10037{_}2842{_}You must be crazy, child!"
10037{_}2843{_}"Their souls are white, Aunt Kate, and there is no color line on the Rock of Ages."
10037{_}2844{_}"Oh, well, tastes differ," said her aunt carelessly, "but it is a strange fancy for Judge Hildreth's niece.
10037{_}2845{_}Next thing you will suggest going to board with Pompey."
10037{_}2846{_}"I might fare a good deal worse," said Evadne with her soft laugh.
10037{_}2847{_}"Dyce keeps her rooms like waxwork and she is a capital cook."
10037{_}2848{_}"Really, Evadne, I am in despair!
10037{_}2849{_}You have not an iota of proper pride.
10037{_}2850{_}How are you going to maintain your position in society?"
10037{_}2851{_}"I don't believe I care to test the question, Aunt Kate; but I think my position will maintain itself."
10037{_}2852{_}"Well said, Evadne," said her uncle, looking up from his paper.
10037{_}2853{_}"You will never forget you are a Hildreth, eh?"
10037{_}2854{_}"Higher than that, uncle," said Evadne softly.
10037{_}2855{_}"I am a sister of Jesus Christ."
10037{_}2856{_}"I don't know what to make of the child," said Mrs. Hildreth discontentedly, as the door closed behind her.
10037{_}2857{_}"I believe she would rather associate with such people than with those of her own class.
10037{_}2858{_}She has a bowing acquaintance with the most _outre_ looking individuals I ever saw.
10037{_}2859{_}I really don't think Dr. Jerome is wise setting young girls to visit in the German quarter.
10037{_}2860{_}It doesn't hurt Marion, now.
10037{_}2861{_}She only does it as a disagreeable duty and is immensely relieved when her round of visits is made for the month, but Evadne takes as much interest in them as if they were her relations.
10037{_}2862{_}Next thing we know, she will be wanting to take up slum work.
10037{_}2863{_}I hope she won't come to any harm down among those crazy blacks.
10037{_}2864{_}They always seem to get possessed the moment they touch religion."
10037{_}2865{_}"I do not think Evadne will ever come to any harm," the Judge said slowly.
10037{_}2866{_}"The Lord takes pretty good care of his own."
10037{_}2867{_}His wife looked at him with a puzzled expression.
10037{_}2868{_}"I fully intended going to prayer meeting myself to-night," she said, "but it gets to be a great tax,--an evening out of every week,--and I do dread the night air so much."
10037{_}2869{_}Mrs. Judge Hildreth dipped her jeweled fingers into the perfumed water of her finger glass and dried them on her silk-fringed napkin.
10037{_}2870{_}"Oh, Lawrence, don't forget Judge Tracer's dinner to-morrow night.
10037{_}2871{_}You will have to come home earlier than usual, for it is such a long drive, and it will never do to keep his mulligatawny waiting.
10037{_}2872{_}And, by the way, I made a new engagement for you to-day.
10037{_}2873{_}Mrs. General Leighton has invited us to join the Shakespearean Club which she is getting up.
10037{_}2874{_}It is to be very select.
10037{_}2875{_}Will meet at the different houses, you know, with a choice little supper at the close.
10037{_}2876{_}She says the one she belonged to in Atlanta was a brilliant affair.
10037{_}2877{_}She comes from one of Georgia's first families, you remember."
10037{_}2878{_}"A Shakespearean Club!"
10037{_}2879{_}and Judge Hildreth smiled incredulously.
10037{_}2880{_}"Why, my dear, I never knew you and the immortal Will had much affinity for each other!"
10037{_}2881{_}"Oh, of course it is more for the prestige of the thing.
10037{_}2882{_}Mrs. Leighton said the General assured her you would never find leisure for it, but I said I would promise for you.
10037{_}2883{_}It is only one evening a week you know.
10037{_}2884{_}She thinks we Americans retire far too early from the enjoyments of life in favor of our children, and I believe she is right.
10037{_}2885{_}I certainly do not feel myself in the sere and yellow," and Mrs. Judge Hildreth regarded herself complacently in the long mirror before which she stood.
10037{_}2886{_}"You will manage to make the time, Lawrence?"
10037{_}2887{_}"What other answer but 'yes' can Petruchio make to 'the prettiest Kate in Christendom'?"
10037{_}2888{_}replied the Judge, bowing gallantly to the face in the mirror as he came up and stood beside his wife.
10037{_}2889{_}It was a handsome face but there was a hardness about it, and the lines around the mouth which bespoke an indomitable will, had deepened with the years.
10037{_}2890{_}"Only one evening a week, Kate, but you thought that too much of a tax just now."
10037{_}2891{_}"How absurd you are, Lawrence!
10037{_}2892{_}When shall I make you understand that there are sacrifices that must be made.
10037{_}2893{_}We owe a duty to society.
10037{_}2894{_}We cannot afford to let ourselves drop wholly out of the world."
10037{_}2895{_}A little later Judge Hildreth entered his library with a heavy sigh.
10037{_}2896{_}He had attained the ends he had striven for, he was respected alike in the church and the world, he held a high and lucrative position, he had a well appointed home, over which his handsome wife presided with dignity and grace, and yet, as he took his seat before his desk in the lofty room whose shelves were lined with gems of thought in fragrant, costly bindings, life seemed to have missed its sweetness to Lawrence Hildreth.
10037{_}2897{_}Evadne's words haunted him, and, like an accusing angel, the letter which still lay hidden under the mass of papers in the drawer which he never opened, seemed to look at him reproachfully.
10037{_}2898{_}"A sister of Jesus Christ."
10037{_}2899{_}Sisters and brothers lived together.
10037{_}2900{_}Was it possible that Jesus Christ could be in this house,--this very room?
10037{_}2901{_}The idea was appalling.
10037{_}2902{_}He was familiar with the truism that God was everywhere, but he had never really believed it; and, as the years passed, he had found it convenient to remove him to a shadowy distance in space, less likely to interfere with modern business methods.
10037{_}2903{_}Jesus Christ, enshrined in a far off glory among his angels, appealed to the decorum of his religious sentiment; but Jesus Christ, face to face, to be reckoned with in the practical details of honesty and fair dealing; that was a different matter.
10037{_}2904{_}And this was the violation of a dead man's trust, who had put everything in his power because he had faith in him!
10037{_}2905{_}He saw again the young brother, handsome, easy-going to a fault, but with a sense of honor so fine as to shrink in indignation from the slightest breath of shame; read again the closing words of the farewell letter which he had read for the first time on the day now so long ago, which he would have given worlds to recall, and which, from out the shadowy recesses of eternity, laughed at his futile wish.
10037{_}2906{_}"So, my dear brother," the letter ran, "I am giving you this responsibility as only a brother can.
10037{_}2907{_}I have left Evadne absolutely untrammelled.
10037{_}2908{_}I have no fear that my little girl will abuse the trust.
10037{_}2909{_}She is wise beyond her years, with a sense of honor as keen as your own."
10037{_}2910{_}The Judge's head sank upon his hands.
10037{_}2911{_}It was for Evadne's good he had persuaded himself.
10037{_}2912{_}She was too much of a child,--and now,--the letter could not be delivered.
10037{_}2913{_}It meant disgrace and shame.
10037{_}2914{_}It was his duty as a father to shield his family from that.
10037{_}2915{_}How well he could picture Evadne's look of bewildered, incredulous surprise, and then the pain, tinged with scorn, which would creep into the clear eyes.
10037{_}2916{_}And Jesus Christ!
10037{_}2917{_}The Judge's head sank lower as he heard the voice which has rung down through the ages in scathing denunciation of all subterfuge and lies.
10037{_}2918{_}"Woe unto you ... hypocrites!
10037{_}2919{_}for ye tithe mint and anise and cummin, and have left undone the weightier matters of the law, justice and mercy and faith."
10037{_}2920{_}"Woe unto you ... hypocrites!
10037{_}2921{_}for ye cleanse the outside of the cup and of the platter, but within they are full from extortion and excess."
10037{_}2922{_}"Woe unto you ... hypocrites!
10037{_}2923{_}for ye are like unto whited sepulchres which outwardly appear beautiful, but inwardly are full of dead men's bones."
10037{_}2924{_}Lower and lower sank the Judge's head, until at last it rested upon the desk with a groan.
10037{_}2925{_}*       *       *       *       *  They were singing when Evadne reached the humble church which Dyce and Pompey called their spiritual home.
10037{_}2926{_}The walls were white-washed and the seats were hard, for the "Disciples of Jesus" possessed but little of this world's goods.
10037{_}2927{_}Two prayers followed, full of rich imagery and fervid passion, and then a young girl with a deep contralto voice began to sing,--    "Steal away, steal away,     Steal away to Jesus!
10037{_}2928{_}Steal away, steal away home,     We ain't got long to stay here."
10037{_}2929{_}The soft, deep notes of the weird melody ended in a burst of triumph, and Evadne bent her head while her tired heart thrilled with joy.
10037{_}2930{_}When she looked up again Dyce was speaking.
10037{_}2931{_}"I've ben thinkin', friens," she said, "that we don't get the sweetness of them words inter our hearts ez we should.
10037{_}2932{_}We'se too much taken up wid de thought of de heavenly manshuns to 'member dat de King's chillen hez an inheritance on de earth.
10037{_}2933{_}We'se not poor, lonesome people widout a home!
10037{_}2934{_}De dear Christ promised, 'I will not leave youse orphans, I will come to youse,' an' he who hez de Lord Jesus alongside, hez de best of company.
10037{_}2935{_}'Pears like we don't let our Father's message go any deeper dan de top of our heads.
10037{_}2936{_}Ef we believes we'se preshus in his sight,--an' de Bible sez we is,--we'll hev no occashun fer gettin discouraged, fer de dear Lord's boun ter do de best fer his loved ones.
10037{_}2937{_}Ef we'se keepin' company wid Jesus we'se no call ter want de worl's invitashuns, an ef we'se hidden away in Christ's heart dere's no need fer us ter be frettin' about de little worriments of earth.
10037{_}2938{_}Satan don't hev no chance where Jesus is.
10037{_}2939{_}Ef we'se tempted, friens, an' fall inter sin, it's 'cause we'se not livin' close ter de Saviour.
10037{_}2940{_}"I knows we allers tinks of a home as a place where dere is good times, an' dere don't seem much good times goin' for some of us in dis worl', but dere ain't no call fer us ter spec' ter be better off dan our Lord, an ef we'se feedin' on de Lord Jesus all de time we won't min' ef de worl's bread is scarce; de soul ain't dependin' on dem tings fer nourishmen' an' de Lord Jesus makes de hard bed easy an' de coarse food taste good.
10037{_}2941{_}"'Tain't good management fer us ter be allers groanin' in dis worl' while we 'spect ter be singin' de glory song up yonder.
10037{_}2942{_}De best singers is dem dat's longes' trainin' an' I'se feared some of us'll find it drefful hard ter git up ter de proper concert pitch in heaven ef we sings nuthin but lamentashuns on earth.
10037{_}2943{_}De dear Lord don't seem ter hev made any sort of pervishun for fault findin'.
10037{_}2944{_}He 'low dere'll be trubble, but he tells us ter be of good cheer on account of hevin' him ter git de victry fer us, an' ef we keep singin' all de time, dere ain't no time fer sighs.
10037{_}2945{_}Let us keep a-whisperin' to our Father, my friens.
10037{_}2946{_}It's a beautiful worl' he's put us in, an' dere ain't no combine ter keep us back from enjoyin' de best tings in it.
10037{_}2947{_}De sky belong ter us ez much as to de rich folks, an' de grass an' de trees an' de birds an' de flowers; de rollin rivers an' de mighty ocean belongs ter us.
10037{_}2948{_}De only priviluge de rich folks hez is dat dey kin sail on deir billows while we hez ter stan' alongside,--but dey's powerfu' unhappy sometimes when dey hez so much ter look after, an' we kin enjoy lookin' at deir fine houses widout hevin' any of de care.
10037{_}2949{_}"We'se not payin' much complimen' ter Jesus, friens, when we 'low dat de good tings of dis worl' kin make people happier dan he kin, an' 'pears like we ought ter be 'shamed of ourselves.
10037{_}2950{_}De Bible sez we'se ter 'live an' move an' hev our bein' in God,' an' it don't 'pear becomin' when we hev such a home pervided fer us, ter be allers grumblin' 'cause we can't live in de brown stone fronts an' keep a kerridge.
10037{_}2951{_}We don't begin ter understan' how ter live up ter our privilegus, friens, an' I'se bowed in shame as I tink how de dear Lord's heart must ache as he sees how little we'se appresheatin' his lovin' kindness."
10037{_}2952{_}The tender, pleading voice ceased and then Dyce lifted her clasped hands,--"Oh, Lord Jesus, help us ter glorify thee before de worl'.
10037{_}2953{_}Help us ter understan' an 'preciate de wonderful honor thou hez put upon us.
10037{_}2954{_}Make us used ter dwellin' wid thee on de earth, so as we won't feel like strangers in heaven.
10037{_}2955{_}Oh, blessed Jesus, by de remembrance of de thorn marks an' de nail prints an' de woun' in thy side forgive thy ungrateful chillen.
10037{_}2956{_}We'se ben a' lookin' roun on de perishin' tings of earth fer our comfort, an' a' seekin' our homes in this worl'.
10037{_}2957{_}Lord, help us ter find our real home in thee!
10037{_}2958{_}Help us ter steal away ter Jesus, when de storm cloud hangs low and de billows roar about our heads.
10037{_}2959{_}Dere's no shadows in de home thou makes, fer 'de light of de worl' is Jesus,' an' ebery room is full of de sunshine of thy love.
10037{_}2960{_}Dere's no harm kin cum to us ef we'se inside de fold, fer thou art de door, Lord Jesus; dere's no danger kin touch us ef we'se hidden in de cleft of de rock.
10037{_}2961{_}Lord, make us abide in de secret place of de Almighty an' hoi' us close forever under de shadow of thy wing."
10037{_}2962{_}Then the congregation dispersed to the humble homes, glorified now by the possibility of being made the dwelling-place of the King of kings.
10037{_}2963{_}CHAPTER XVII.
10037{_}2964{_}It was intensely warm in the Marlborough Steel Works.
10037{_}2965{_}Outdoors the sun beat fiercely upon the heads of toiling men and horses while the heat waves danced with a dazzling shimmer along the brick pavements.
10037{_}2966{_}Indoors there was the steady thud of the engine, and the great hammers clanked and the belts swept through the air with a deafening whirr, while the workmen drew blackened hands across their grimy foreheads and John Randolph gave a sigh of longing for the cool forest chambers of Hollywood, as he leaned over to exchange a cheery word with Richard Trueman, beside whom he had been working for over a year and for whom he had come to entertain a strong feeling of affection.
10037{_}2967{_}Varied experiences had come to him since he had said good-by to his kind Quaker friends and started on his search for work.
10037{_}2968{_}Monotonous days of wood piling in a lumber yard, long weeks of isolation among the giant trees of the forest, where no sound was to be heard except the whistle of the axes, as they cleaved the air, and the coarse jokes of the workmen,--then had come days when even odd jobs had been hailed with delight, and he had sat at the feet of the grim schoolmistress Necessity and learned how little man really needs to have to live.
10037{_}2969{_}And then the Steel Works had opened again and he had forged his way up through the different departments to the responsible position he now held.
10037{_}2970{_}His promotion had been rapid.
10037{_}2971{_}The foreman had been quick to note the keen, intelligent interest and deft-handedness of this strangely alert new employe.
10037{_}2972{_}He finished his work in the very best way that it was possible to do it, even though it took a little longer in the doing.
10037{_}2973{_}Such workmen were not common at the Marlborough Steel Works.
10037{_}2974{_}He put his heart into whatever he did.
10037{_}2975{_}That was John Randolph's way.
10037{_}2976{_}There was something about the work which pleased him.
10037{_}2977{_}It gave him a feeling of triumph to watch the evolution of the crude chaos into the finished perfection, and see how through baptism of fire and flood the diverse particles emerged at length a beautifully tempered whole.
10037{_}2978{_}He read as in an allegory the discipline which a soul needs to fit it for the kingdom, and so throughout the meshes of his daily toil John Randolph wove his parable.
10037{_}2979{_}When evening came he would stride cheerily along the dingy street to the house where he and his fellow-workman lodged, refresh himself with a hot bath, don what he called his dress suit, and after their simple meal and a frolic with little Dick, the motherless boy who was the joy of Richard Trueman's heart, he would settle down for a long evening of study among his cherished books.
10037{_}2980{_}John Randolph never lost sight of the fact that he was to be a physician by and by.
10037{_}2981{_}*       *       *       *       *  Somewhere in one of the great centers of the world's industry a workman had blundered.
10037{_}2982{_}His conscience urged him to confess his mistake, while Satan whispered with a sneer,--"Yes, and get turned adrift for your pains, with a rating into the bargain!"
10037{_}2983{_}"Never mind if you do lose a week's wages," conscience had pleaded, "your hands will be clean," and the workman shrugged his shoulders with a muttered, "Pshaw!
10037{_}2984{_}What do I care for that, so long as I don't git found out.
10037{_}2985{_}I'll fix it so as no one kin tell it was me."
10037{_}2986{_}The work was passed upon by the foreman and the Company's certificate attached.
10037{_}2987{_}The man chuckled, "Hooray!
10037{_}2988{_}Now that it's out from under old Daggett's eyes nobody'll ever be able to lay the blame on me!"
10037{_}2989{_}and he had gone home whistling.
10037{_}2990{_}He forgot God!
10037{_}2991{_}*       *       *       *       *  The long, stifling day was drawing near its close.
10037{_}2992{_}Half an hour more and the workmen would be free to rest.
10037{_}2993{_}Only half an hour!
10037{_}2994{_}Suddenly there was a sharp clicking sound, then a cry, and in an instant all was bustle and confusion at the Marlborough Steel Works.
10037{_}2995{_}The great hammers hung suspended in mid-air, the whirling wheels were still, while the workmen, with faces showing pale beneath the grime, gathered hastily around a fallen comrade.
10037{_}2996{_}Summoned by telephone the Company's surgeon was driving rapidly towards the Works, but his services would not be required.
10037{_}2997{_}An accident.
10037{_}2998{_}No one knew just how it happened.
10037{_}2999{_}There must have been a flaw, a defect in some part of the machinery.
10037{_}3000{_}These things do happen.
10037{_}3001{_}Somewhere there had been carelessness, dishonesty, and the price of it was--a life!
10037{_}3002{_}The dying man opened his eyes suddenly and looked full at John Randolph, who knelt beside him supporting his head on his arm.
10037{_}3003{_}"Little Dick," he murmured.
10037{_}3004{_}"All right, Trueman, I will take care of him."
10037{_}3005{_}"God bless you, John!"
10037{_}3006{_}and with the fervid benediction, the breath ceased and the spirit flew away.
10037{_}3007{_}The body was prepared for the inquest, and through the gathering dusk John, strangely white and silent, entered the house he called home, gathered the fatherless boy into his arms and let him sob out his grief upon his shoulder.
10037{_}3008{_}*       *       *       *       *  Some days after the funeral the Manager sent for John to come to his private office.
10037{_}3009{_}He was a pleasant man and had taken a kindly interest in the capable young workman from the start.
10037{_}3010{_}"Well, Randolph, this is a terrible business of poor Trueman," he said, as he pointed him to a chair.
10037{_}3011{_}"Terrible!
10037{_}3012{_}I can't get over it.
10037{_}3013{_}A fine man and one of our best finishers too.
10037{_}3014{_}Well, we can't do anything for him now, poor fellow, but he left a boy I think?"
10037{_}3015{_}"Yes, sir," said John simply; "I have taken him to live with me."
10037{_}3016{_}"Shake hands, Randolph!
10037{_}3017{_}We _talk_ about what ought to be done and you _do_ it.
10037{_}3018{_}Is that your usual mode of procedure?"
10037{_}3019{_}John laughed.
10037{_}3020{_}"There was nothing else to do," he said.
10037{_}3021{_}"H'm.
10037{_}3022{_}Most fellows in your position would have thought it was the last thing possible.
10037{_}3023{_}Have you any idea what it means to saddle yourself with a child like this?
10037{_}3024{_}Whatever put such an idea into your head?"
10037{_}3025{_}"Jesus Christ," answered John quietly.
10037{_}3026{_}"Well, well, you're a queer fellow, Randolph.
10037{_}3027{_}But how are you going to make the wages spin out?
10037{_}3028{_}A boy is 'a growing giant of wants whom the coat of Have is never large enough to cover.'"
10037{_}3029{_}"His father managed, so can I."
10037{_}3030{_}John's voice shook a little.
10037{_}3031{_}"His father!
10037{_}3032{_}But he _was_ his father, you see.
10037{_}3033{_}That makes a mighty difference.
10037{_}3034{_}Well, Randolph, I give you up.
10037{_}3035{_}You are beyond me."
10037{_}3036{_}John rose.
10037{_}3037{_}"Was that all you wished to say to me, Mr.
10037{_}3038{_}Branford?"
10037{_}3039{_}"Sit down, man!
10037{_}3040{_}What the mischief are you in such a hurry for?
10037{_}3041{_}It stands to reason the Company can't let you bear the brunt of this most deplorable occurrence, though I don't believe we could have found a better guardian for the poor little lad.
10037{_}3042{_}But guardians expect to be paid for their trouble.
10037{_}3043{_}What price do you set, Randolph?"
10037{_}3044{_}"I don't want any pay for obeying my Master, Mr.
10037{_}3045{_}Branford."
10037{_}3046{_}"Your Master, Randolph?"
10037{_}3047{_}said the Manager with a puzzled stare.
10037{_}3048{_}"Yes, sir, Jesus Christ."
10037{_}3049{_}"Upon my word, Randolph, you're a queer fellow!
10037{_}3050{_}Well, if you don't want pay, I want some one with a head on his shoulders in this office.
10037{_}3051{_}Any of the fellows in the outside office would be glad of the chance to get in here, but I want a man who understands what he is doing as well as I do myself.
10037{_}3052{_}You have practical knowledge, Randolph, you're the man I want.
10037{_}3053{_}I shall expect you to start in here tomorrow morning.
10037{_}3054{_}The salary will be double your present wages.
10037{_}3055{_}And, since you have constituted yourself guardian of the boy, I may as well tell you that the Company has decided to set aside a yearly sum for his maintenance and education.
10037{_}3056{_}"Now you can go, if you are in such a tremendous hurry, Randolph: only don't try any more of such toploftiness with me.
10037{_}3057{_}It won't go down, you see;" and the Manager chuckled softly, as John, with broken thanks, left the room.
10037{_}3058{_}"I rather think I got the better of him that time!"
10037{_}3059{_}he said to himself.
10037{_}3060{_}CHAPTER XVIII.
10037{_}3061{_}Judge Hildreth sat in his private office, immersed in anxious thought.
10037{_}3062{_}Every day brought new difficulties to be wrestled with in connection with the multitudinous schemes which were making an old man of him while he was still in his prime.
10037{_}3063{_}His hair was grey, his hands trembled, his eyes were bloodshot, and his face had the unhealthy pallor which accompanies intense nervous pressure and excitement.
10037{_}3064{_}He knew that it was so, and the knowledge did not tend to sweeten his disposition.
10037{_}3065{_}He told himself again and again that he could not help it,--it was the force of circumstances and the curse of competition.
10037{_}3066{_}Like the fly in the spider's parlor, he found himself inextricably enveloped in the silken maze of deceit which he had entered so blithely years ago.
10037{_}3067{_}He had ceased to question bitterly whether the game was worth the candle.
10037{_}3068{_}He told himself the Fates had decreed it, and the game had to be played out to the end, The principal thing now was to keep the pieces moving and prevent a checkmate, for that would mean ruin!
10037{_}3069{_}One of the office boys knocked at the door and presented a card, for into this _sanctum sanctorum_ no one was permitted to enter unannounced.
10037{_}3070{_}The card bore the name of the nominal president of the Consolidated Provident Savings Company, which was one of the numerous schemes that Judge Hildreth had on hand.
10037{_}3071{_}It was not always wise to have his name appear.
10037{_}3072{_}He believed in sleeping partnerships.
10037{_}3073{_}As he explained it to himself, that gave one a free hand.
10037{_}3074{_}The Consolidated Provident Savings Company was a popular institution in Marlborough.
10037{_}3075{_}There were conservative financiers who shook their heads and feared that its methods were not based on sound business principles and savored too much of wild-cat schemes and fraudulent speculations, but they were voted cranks by the majority, and the Consolidated Provident Savings Company grew and flourished.
10037{_}3076{_}It paid large dividends, and its stockholders were duly impressed with the magnificence of its buildings and the grandiose tone of its officials.
10037{_}3077{_}Judge Hildreth frowned heavily as he read the name, and was about to deny himself to the visitor, but on second thought he curtly ordered the boy to show him in.
10037{_}3078{_}The man who obeyed the invitation bowed deferentially to his chief and then took a chair in front of him, with the table between.
10037{_}3079{_}He was elaborately dressed, and the shiny silk hat which he deposited on the table looked aggressively prosperous.
10037{_}3080{_}His manner betokened a man suddenly inflated with a sense of his own importance.
10037{_}3081{_}His hair was sandy, and the thin moustache and beard failed to cover the pitifully weak lines of his mouth and chin.
10037{_}3082{_}"Good-morning, Peters."
10037{_}3083{_}The Judge nodded carelessly as he spoke, but he moved uneasily in his chair.
10037{_}3084{_}Of late the sight of this man fretted him.
10037{_}3085{_}It seemed as if he always saw him accompanied by a ghostly form.
10037{_}3086{_}He tried to shake off the impression, and told himself angrily that he was falling into his dotage; but his memory would not yield.
10037{_}3087{_}He saw again the pleading, trustful face of the man's mother as, years ago, she had besought him to do what he could for her son.
10037{_}3088{_}"Just make a man of him, like yourself, Judge Hildreth," she had pleaded.
10037{_}3089{_}"I will be more than satisfied then.
10037{_}3090{_}I want my boy to be respected and to have a place in the world.
10037{_}3091{_}Folks needn't know how hard his mother had to work."
10037{_}3092{_}The Judge smiled grimly as he thought of her phrasing,--"a man like yourself."
10037{_}3093{_}She did not know how near to it he had come!
10037{_}3094{_}The boy had a surface smartness, and he had proved himself an apt scholar.
10037{_}3095{_}The Judge had found him a willing tool in many of his deep laid schemes to get money for less than money's worth.
10037{_}3096{_}But within the last few months there had been a change.
10037{_}3097{_}A spark of manhood had asserted itself, and in the presence of his minion the Judge found himself upon the rack.
10037{_}3098{_}He was the first to speak.
10037{_}3099{_}"I hope there is nothing out of the usual?"
10037{_}3100{_}he said.
10037{_}3101{_}"I intended coming over to the office before the meeting of directors took place."
10037{_}3102{_}"It is the same old trouble about bonds, Judge Hildreth.
10037{_}3103{_}There are not enough of them to go round."
10037{_}3104{_}The Judge rubbed his hands in simulated pleasure.
10037{_}3105{_}"Well, that shows good management, Peters, if the public are hungry for our stock."
10037{_}3106{_}"The public are fools!"
10037{_}3107{_}said the young man, hotly.
10037{_}3108{_}"Not at all, Peters.
10037{_}3109{_}A discriminating public, you know, always chooses the best depositaries."
10037{_}3110{_}He chuckled softly.
10037{_}3111{_}He had turned his eyes towards the window so as not to see the ghostly figure behind the young man's chair which had such a world of reproach in its face.
10037{_}3112{_}"There is only one thing to do, Peters.
10037{_}3113{_}We must water it a little, eh?"
10037{_}3114{_}"It seems to me we've been using the watering-pot rather too frequently."
10037{_}3115{_}The Judge started.
10037{_}3116{_}Had he detected a menace in the tone?
10037{_}3117{_}He temporized.
10037{_}3118{_}His plans were not sufficiently matured yet.
10037{_}3119{_}When they were he would crush this tool of his as surely and as carelessly as he would have crushed a fly.
10037{_}3120{_}"Nonsense, Peters!"
10037{_}3121{_}he said pleasantly; "that is only a little clever financing to tide us over the hard places.
10037{_}3122{_}Of course we will make it all good to the public--by and bye."
10037{_}3123{_}"How?"
10037{_}3124{_}The question rang out through the office like a pistol shot.
10037{_}3125{_}The Judge looked at the man before him in amaze.
10037{_}3126{_}For once his face showed determination and an honest purpose.
10037{_}3127{_}"Will you tell me how we're going to do it?"
10037{_}3128{_}he persisted with a strange vehemence.
10037{_}3129{_}"I've been a fool, Judge Hildreth, a blamed, gigantic fool!
10037{_}3130{_}I've let you hood wink me and lead me by the nose for years.
10037{_}3131{_}I've done your dirty work for you and borne the credit of it, too; but I swear I'll not do it any longer.
10037{_}3132{_}I thought at first--fool that I was--that everything you did was just the right thing to copy.
10037{_}3133{_}My poor old mother told me you were the pattern I was to follow if I wanted to be an honorable man.
10037{_}3134{_}An honorable man!
10037{_}3135{_}Good heavens!
10037{_}3136{_}"Do you know where I've been these last months?
10037{_}3137{_}I've been in hell, sir; in hell, I tell you!
10037{_}3138{_}Every night I've dreamed of my mother and every day I've bamboozled the public and sold bonds that weren't worth the paper they were written on, and paid big dividends that were just some of their own money returned.
10037{_}3139{_}And now you tell me to keep on watering the stock when you know we haven't a dollar put towards the 'Rest' and the money is just pouring out for expenses and directors' fees.
10037{_}3140{_}There's barely enough left over to keep up the sham of dividends.
10037{_}3141{_}You know it as well as I do.
10037{_}3142{_}I've been an ass and an idiot, but I'm done with living a lie.
10037{_}3143{_}Judge Hildreth, I came to tell you that if you don't do the square thing by these people who have trusted us, I'll expose you!"
10037{_}3144{_}His vehemence was tremendous and the words poured out in a torrent which never checked its flow.
10037{_}3145{_}He had risen and in his excitement paced up and down the room.
10037{_}3146{_}Now, overcome by his effort, he sank exhausted into a chair.
10037{_}3147{_}Judge Hildreth rose suddenly and locked the office door.
10037{_}3148{_}When he turned again his face was not a pleasant sight to see.
10037{_}3149{_}"President Peters," he said sternly, "this is not the age of heroics nor the place for them.
10037{_}3150{_}In future I beg you to remember our relative positions.
10037{_}3151{_}You seem to forget that I am the direct cause of your present prosperity, but that is an omission which men of your stamp are liable to make.
10037{_}3152{_}I never expect gratitude from those whom I have befriended.
10037{_}3153{_}"But when you come to threats, that is another matter.
10037{_}3154{_}You say you will expose me.
10037{_}3155{_}To whom, if you please?
10037{_}3156{_}_You_ are the President of the Consolidated Company.
10037{_}3157{_}Your name is associated with its business.
10037{_}3158{_}Mine does not appear in any way, shape or form.
10037{_}3159{_}You sign all papers, and it is you whom the public hold accountable for all moneys deposited in the institution.
10037{_}3160{_}Any attempt which you might make to connect me with the enterprise would be futile, utterly futile.
10037{_}3161{_}The public would not believe you, and you could not prove it in any court of law."
10037{_}3162{_}The man, worn and spent with his emotion, lifted his head and looked at the Judge with dazed, lack-luster eyes.
10037{_}3163{_}"Not connected with the enterprise," he repeated, "why, the whole thought of the thing came from you!
10037{_}3164{_}and you have drawn thousands of dollars----"  "I have simply given advice," interrupted the Judge haughtily.
10037{_}3165{_}"Advice!"
10037{_}3166{_}echoed the man, "and doesn't advice count in law?"
10037{_}3167{_}"If you can prove it;" said the Judge with a cold smile.
10037{_}3168{_}"Do you ever remember having any of my opinions in writing, President Peters?
10037{_}3169{_}The law takes cognizance only of black and white, you know."
10037{_}3170{_}The victim writhed in his chair, as the trap in which he was caught revealed itself.
10037{_}3171{_}Heavily his eyes searched Judge Hildreth's face for some sign of pity or relenting, but in vain.
10037{_}3172{_}"And if there should come a run on the funds?"
10037{_}3173{_}he questioned dully.
10037{_}3174{_}"If there should come a run on the funds," answered the Judge, "_you_ would be underneath."
10037{_}3175{_}The man's head fell forward upon the table, and the Judge, with a cruel smile, left the room.
10037{_}3176{_}*       *       *       *       *  Two office boys lingered in the handsome offices of the Consolidated Provident Savings Company after business hours were over.
10037{_}3177{_}"I tell you what it is, Bob," said the eldest one, "I'm going to quit this concern.
10037{_}3178{_}It's my opinion it's a rotten corporation; and I don't propose to ruin my standing with the commercial world."
10037{_}3179{_}"Gee!"
10037{_}3180{_}exclaimed the younger boy in delight.
10037{_}3181{_}"You're a buster, Joe, and no mistake.
10037{_}3182{_}The president himself couldn't have rolled that sentence off better, or that old piece of pomposity who conies to the secret meetings with the gold-headed cane."
10037{_}3183{_}"That's Judge Hildreth.
10037{_}3184{_}He's another deep one or I lose my guess."
10037{_}3185{_}"Why, he's a No.
10037{_}3186{_}I deacon in one of the uptown's swellest churches!"
10037{_}3187{_}"Guess he's a child of darkness in between times then, for I'll bet he does lots of underground work.
10037{_}3188{_}I don't believe in this awfully private business.
10037{_}3189{_}The other day, after old man Hildreth came, before the directors had their meeting, (he always does come just before that, to prime Peters, you know,) what did he do but make Peters send for me to shut the transoms over his office doors, so that none of us fellows outside could hear what they were saying!
10037{_}3190{_}"I tell you I don't like the looks of things.
10037{_}3191{_}This morning one of those heavy stockholders came in and wanted to take out all his money, and the president went white as a sheet.
10037{_}3192{_}There's a flaw in the ready money account somewhere, I'll bet, and I'm going to leave before the bottom drops out of the concern.
10037{_}3193{_}If you take my advice you'll follow."
10037{_}3194{_}The other boy laughed.
10037{_}3195{_}"Bet your life I won't, then.
10037{_}3196{_}Where'd you get such good pay, I'd like to know?
10037{_}3197{_}I've had enough of grubbing along on $4.00 a week.
10037{_}3198{_}No, sirree, I'll keep in tow with the deacon and get my share of all the stuff that's going, same as the other fellows do."
10037{_}3199{_}"You won't do it long then, you mark my words.
10037{_}3200{_}Did you see the president when he came into the office this morning?
10037{_}3201{_}He looked as if he'd been gagged.
10037{_}3202{_}I went into his office for something in a hurry afterwards and he was head over ears in Railway Time Tables.
10037{_}3203{_}He jumped as if he'd been caught poaching.
10037{_}3204{_}It's my belief he means to skip across the border.
10037{_}3205{_}It's the only way for him to get out of the mess, unless he takes a dose of lead, you see.
10037{_}3206{_}"Well, here goes.
10037{_}3207{_}I'm going to write my resignation with the president's best gold pen.
10037{_}3208{_}You can do as you like, but it's slow and honest for me."
10037{_}3209{_}CHAPTER XIX.
10037{_}3210{_}Miss Diana Chillingworth was sitting in the old-fashioned porch of her old-fashioned house which opened into an old-fashioned garden in one of the suburbs of Marlborough, shelling peas.
10037{_}3211{_}Everything about Miss Diana was old-fashioned and sweet.
10037{_}3212{_}Her hair was dressed as she had been accustomed to wear it in her girlhood, and even the head mantua-maker of Marlborough, ardent worshiper at Fashion's shrine though she was, was forced to bow before her gentle individuality and confess that Miss Diana's taste was perfect.
10037{_}3213{_}She wore a morning dress of soft pearl grey, over which she had tied an apron of white lawn with a dainty ruffle of embroidery below its hem.
10037{_}3214{_}The peas danced merrily against the sides of an old-fashioned china bowl.
10037{_}3215{_}Miss Diana had an aesthetic repugnance to the use of tin utensils in the preparation of food.
10037{_}3216{_}Outside there were sweet lilies of the valley and violets and pansies, and the roses wafted long breaths of fragrance to her through the trellis work of the porch, while the morning glories hung their heads and blushed under the ardent kisses of the sun.
10037{_}3217{_}In the kitchen Unavella Cynthesia Crockett, her faithful and devoted "assistant" (Miss Crockett objected to the term servant upon democratic principles), moved cheerily, with a giant masterfulness which bespoke a successful initiation into the mysteries of the culinary art.
10037{_}3218{_}All at once she shut the oven door, where three toothsome loaves were browning, and listened intently.
10037{_}3219{_}Then she went out to interview Thomas, the butcher's boy, who came three times a week with supplies.
10037{_}3220{_}"The sweet-breads hez cum, Miss Di-an," she said, appearing in the porch before her mistress.
10037{_}3221{_}"Well, Unavella," said Miss Diana, with a pleasant smile, "you expected them, did you not?
10037{_}3222{_}We ordered them, you know.
10037{_}3223{_}They are very nutritious, I think."
10037{_}3224{_}"Hum!
10037{_}3225{_}There's some news cum along with 'em that ain't likely to prove ez nourishin'.
10037{_}3226{_}Tummas sez the Provident Savings Company hez busted an' the president's vamoosed."
10037{_}3227{_}"Dear me!
10037{_}3228{_}I wish Thomas would not use such very forceful language," said Miss Diana.
10037{_}3229{_}"Do you think he finds it necessary?
10037{_}3230{_}Being a butcher, you know?
10037{_}3231{_}I hardly understand the words.
10037{_}3232{_}Do you think you would find them defined in Webster?"
10037{_}3233{_}Unavella's eyes twinkled through her gloom.
10037{_}3234{_}"I guess Tummas ain't got much use for dictionners," she said.
10037{_}3235{_}"He uses words that cums nearest to his feelin's.
10037{_}3236{_}He's lost two hundred dollars, Tummas hez."
10037{_}3237{_}"Dear me!
10037{_}3238{_}How very grieved I am.
10037{_}3239{_}But a dictionary, Unavella, is the basis of all education.
10037{_}3240{_}Thomas ought to appreciate that.
10037{_}3241{_}'Busted,'" she repeated the word slowly, with an instinctive shrinking from its sound, "that is a vulgar corruption of the verb to burst; but 'vamoosed,' I do not think I ever heard the term before."
10037{_}3242{_}"Tummas says it means to show the under side of your shoe leather."
10037{_}3243{_}"The under side of your shoe leather, Unavella?"
10037{_}3244{_}Miss Diana lifted her pretty shoe and held it up for inspection.
10037{_}3245{_}"Do you see anything wrong with that?"
10037{_}3246{_}The faithful soul threw her apron over her head with a sob.
10037{_}3247{_}"Oh, Miss Di-an!"
10037{_}3248{_}she wailed, "it means the company's all a set of cheats, an' the biggest rogue of the lot hez lit out--run away--an' taken the money the Gin'rel left you along with him."
10037{_}3249{_}CHAPTER XX.
10037{_}3250{_}Miss Diana received the news in absolute silence.
10037{_}3251{_}The brave daughter of a brave father, she would make no moan, but the sweetness seemed to have suddenly gone from the flowers and the light out of the sky.
10037{_}3252{_}Unavella looked at her in amazement.
10037{_}3253{_}She was used to the stormy grief which finds vent in tears and groans.
10037{_}3254{_}"It beats me how different folks takes things!"
10037{_}3255{_}she ejaculated mentally.
10037{_}3256{_}"Well, she'll need suthin' to keep her strength up all the more now she ain't got nuthin' to support her;" and, gathering peas and pods into her apron with a mighty sweep of her arm, she marched into her kitchen in a fever of sympathetic indignation and evolved a dinner which was a masterpiece of culinary skill.
10037{_}3257{_}Miss Diana forced herself to eat something.
10037{_}3258{_}She knew if she did not, Unavella would be worried, and she possessed that peculiar regard for the feelings of others which would not allow her to consider her own.
10037{_}3259{_}"You are a wonderful cook, Unavella," she said, with a pathetic cheerfulness which did not deceive her faithful handmaiden, who, as she confided afterwards to a friend, wuz weepin' bitter gall tears in her mind, though she kep' a calm front outside, for she wuzn't goin' ter be outdid in pluck by that little bit of sweetness.
10037{_}3260{_}"I shall be able to give you a beautiful character."
10037{_}3261{_}She lifted her hand with a deprecating gesture as Unavella was about to burst forth with a stormy denial.
10037{_}3262{_}"Not yet, please, Unavella; not just yet.
10037{_}3263{_}Let me have time to think a little before you say anything.
10037{_}3264{_}I feel rather shaken.
10037{_}3265{_}The news was so very unexpected, you see," she said with a shadowy smile, which Unavella averred "cut her heart clean in two."
10037{_}3266{_}"But everything is just right, Unavella, that happens to the Lord's children, you know.
10037{_}3267{_}Things look a little misty now, but I shall see the sunlight again by and bye.
10037{_}3268{_}In the meantime there is this delicious dinner.
10037{_}3269{_}Someone ought to be reaping the benefit of it.
10037{_}3270{_}Suppose you take it to poor Mrs. Dixon?
10037{_}3271{_}She enjoys anything tasty so much and she cannot afford to buy dainties for herself."
10037{_}3272{_}Miss Diana would never learn the economy which is content to be comfortable while a neighbor is in need.
10037{_}3273{_}"And, Unavella, if you please, you might say I am not receiving callers this afternoon.
10037{_}3274{_}I am afraid it is not very hospitable, but I feel as if I must be alone.
10037{_}3275{_}This has been rather a sudden shock to me."
10037{_}3276{_}"You, you--angul!"
10037{_}3277{_}exclaimed Unavella, as soon as she had regained the privacy of her kitchen, while a briny crystal of genuine affection rolled down her cheek and splashed unceremoniously into the gravy.
10037{_}3278{_}Up-stairs in her pretty chamber Miss Diana sat and thought.
10037{_}3279{_}Ruin and starvation.
10037{_}3280{_}Was that what it meant?
10037{_}3281{_}She had seen the words in print often but they seemed different now.
10037{_}3282{_}Ruin meant a giving up and going out, while the auctioneer's hammer smote upon one's heart with cruel blows, and one could not see to say farewell because one's eyes were full of tears.
10037{_}3283{_}It would not be starvation--of the body.
10037{_}3284{_}She must be thankful for that.
10037{_}3285{_}The house and grounds were in a good locality and she had refused several handsome offers for them during the past year.
10037{_}3286{_}She caught her breath a little as she thought of the wide stretching field where her dainty Jersey was feeding, with its cluster of trees in one corner, under which a brook babbled joyously as it danced on its way to the river; the pretty barn with its pigeon-house where her snow-white fantails craned their imperious heads; the wide porch with its flower drapery, where she sat and read or worked with her pet spaniel at her feet, and where her friends loved to gather through the summer afternoons and chat over the early supper before they went back to the city's grime and stir.
10037{_}3287{_}Then in thought she entered the house.
10037{_}3288{_}The room which had been her father's and the library which held his books.
10037{_}3289{_}Could she sell those!
10037{_}3290{_}She shivered, as in imagination she heard the careless inventory of the auctioneer.
10037{_}3291{_}She had never attended an auction except once, and then she had hurried away, for it seemed to her the pictured faces were misty with tears and she fancied the draperies sighed, as they waved in the wind which swept through the gaping windows.
10037{_}3292{_}There were the engravings which she loved and the pictures her father had brought with him from Europe, and the rare old china and her mother's silver service, and her store of delicate napery and household linen; while every table and chair had a story and the very walls of each room were dear.
10037{_}3293{_}Had she been making idols of these things in her heart?
10037{_}3294{_}Miss Diana knelt beside the couch, comfortable as only old-fashioned couches know how to be.
10037{_}3295{_}"Dear Christ," she cried, "I am thy follower and I have gone shod with velvet while thy feet were travel-stained, and I have slept upon eider-down while thou hadst not where to lay thine head!"
10037{_}3296{_}She knelt on, motionless, until the twilight fell and the stars began to peep out in the sky.
10037{_}3297{_}Then she went down-stairs and there was a strange, exalted look upon her sweet face.
10037{_}3298{_}"Unavella," she cried softly, "I have found the sunlight, for I can say 'The Lord gave, and the Lord hath taken away; blessed be the name of the LORD.'"
10037{_}3299{_}"Oh, Miss Di-an!"
10037{_}3300{_}wailed Unavella, "I b'lieve you're goin' ter die an' be an angul afore the moon changes!"
10037{_}3301{_}*       *       *       *       *  Miss Diana had been to see her lawyer and he had confirmed her decision.
10037{_}3302{_}Her income was gone.
10037{_}3303{_}With the exception of a couple of hundred dollars, coming to her from a different source, she was penniless.
10037{_}3304{_}There was nothing left her but to sell.
10037{_}3305{_}When she reached home that night she looked very white and weary, but her smile was all the sweeter because of the unshed tears.
10037{_}3306{_}Unavella had spread her supper in the porch.
10037{_}3307{_}She ate but little, however.
10037{_}3308{_}"I am sorry I cannot do more justice to your skill, Unavella," she said with her gentle courtesy, "but I do not seem to feel hungry lately."
10037{_}3309{_}"It's that li-yar!"
10037{_}3310{_}muttered Unavella grimly, as she cleared the things away.
10037{_}3311{_}"I never knowed a li-yar yit that didn't scare all the appetite away from a body."
10037{_}3312{_}When her work was finished she came back to the porch where Miss Diana was sitting very still in the moonlight.
10037{_}3313{_}"Miss Di-an!"
10037{_}3314{_}she exclaimed impetuously, "don't you go fer to be thinkin' of sellin'!
10037{_}3315{_}I've got a plan that beats the li-yar's all holler, ef he duz wear a wig."
10037{_}3316{_}"Sit down, Unavella," said her mistress kindly, "and tell me what it is."
10037{_}3317{_}"Well, I haven't said nuthin' to you before, 'cause I knowed it would only hurt you ef I wuz to let my feelin's loose about them thievin' rapscallions that dared to lay their cheatin' hands on the money the Gin'rel left ye; but I've been a thinkin'--stiddy--an' while you wuz comin' to your decision above I wuz comin' to mine below, an' now we'll toss 'em up fer luck, an' see which wins, ef you air willin'."
10037{_}3318{_}Miss Diana smiled.
10037{_}3319{_}"Well, Unavella."
10037{_}3320{_}she said.
10037{_}3321{_}"You decide ter leave yer hum, with all there is to it, an' me inter the bargain, an' go ter board with folks what don't know yer likins nor understan' yer feelin's, an' the end on it'll be that you'll jest wilt away wuss than a mornin' glory.
10037{_}3322{_}I never did think folks sarved the Lord by dyin' afore their time comes.
10037{_}3323{_}"I decide to hev you keep yer hum, an' the things in it, an' me too.
10037{_}3324{_}The hull on it is, Miss Di-an, _I won't be left_!"
10037{_}3325{_}and Unavella buried her face in her hands and sobbed aloud.
10037{_}3326{_}"You dear Unavella!"
10037{_}3327{_}Miss Diana laid her soft hand upon the toil-roughened ones.
10037{_}3328{_}"If you only knew how I dread the thought of leaving you!
10037{_}3329{_}But what else is there for me to do?"
10037{_}3330{_}"Gentlemen boarders," was the terse reply.
10037{_}3331{_}"Gentlemen boarders!"
10037{_}3332{_}echoed Miss Diana in bewilderment.
10037{_}3333{_}"Yes.
10037{_}3334{_}You catch 'em, an' I'll cook'em.
10037{_}3335{_}We'll begin with two ter see how they eat, an ef we find it don't cost too much ter fatten 'em up, we'll go inter the bizness reglar;" after making which cannibalistic proposition Unavella looked to her mistress for approval.
10037{_}3336{_}"Why, Unavella," said Miss Diana, after the first shock of surprise was over, "I never even dreamed of such a thing!
10037{_}3337{_}It might be possible, if you are willing to undertake it, it is very good of you.
10037{_}3338{_}But we will not make any plans, Unavella, until I talk it over with the Lord.
10037{_}3339{_}If his smile rests upon it, your kindly thought for me will succeed; if not, it would be sure to fail.
10037{_}3340{_}I must have his approval first of all."
10037{_}3341{_}She rose as she spoke and bade her a gentle good-night, and Unavella walked slowly back to her kitchen again.
10037{_}3342{_}"Ef the angul Gabriel," she soliloquized, "starts in ter searchin' the earth this night fer the Lord's chosen ones, there ain't no fear but what he'll cum ter this house, the fust thing."
10037{_}3343{_}Up-stairs Miss Diana was whispering softly, as she looked up at the stars with a trustful smile.
10037{_}3344{_}"Oh, my Father, if it is thy will that I should do this thing, thou wilt send me the right ones."
10037{_}3345{_}CHAPTER XXI.
10037{_}3346{_}John Randolph did some hard thinking during the weeks which followed Richard Trueman's death.
10037{_}3347{_}It was no light task which he had so cheerfully imposed upon himself.
10037{_}3348{_}The boy was constitutionally delicate and fretted so constantly after his father that his health began to suffer, and it grew to be a very pale face which welcomed John with a smile when he returned from the office.
10037{_}3349{_}The style of living was bad for him.
10037{_}3350{_}He was alone all day, except for an occasional visit from the good-natured German woman who kept their rooms, and, although he was a voracious reader, the doctor had forbidden all thought of study for a year, even had there been a school near enough for him to attend, where John would have been willing to send him.
10037{_}3351{_}He ought to be where the air was pure and the surroundings cheerful.
10037{_}3352{_}John would have preferred to put up with the discomfort of his present quarters and lay by the addition to his salary towards the more speedy realization of his day-dream, but John Randolph had never found much time to think of himself; there were always so many other people in the world to be attended to.
10037{_}3353{_}"Dick, my boy," he said cheerily one evening, after they had finished what he pronounced a sumptuous repast, "I have a presentiment that this month will witness a turning point in our career.
10037{_}3354{_}I believe you and I are going to become suburbanites."
10037{_}3355{_}The boy's sad eyes grew wide with wonder.
10037{_}3356{_}"What do you mean, John?"
10037{_}3357{_}"Well you see, Dick True, it is this way.
10037{_}3358{_}As soon as I get my degree--earn the right to put M.D.
10037{_}3359{_}after my name, you know,--I am going to take two rubber bags, fill one with sunshine and one with pure air, full of the scent of rose leaves and clover and strawberries--ah, Dick, you'd like to smell that, wouldn't you?--and carry one in each pocket; then, when my patients come to me for advice, the first dose I shall give them will be out of my rubber bags, and in six cases out of ten I believe they'll get better without any drug at all.
10037{_}3360{_}You see, Dick True, the trouble is, our Father has given us a whole world full of air and sunlight to be happy in, and we poison the air with smoke and shut ourselves away from the sunshine in boxes of brick and mortar, only letting a stray beam come in occasionally through slits in the walls which we call windows.
10037{_}3361{_}It's no wonder we are such poor, miserable concerns.
10037{_}3362{_}You can't fancy an Indian suffering from nervous prostration, can you, Dick?
10037{_}3363{_}and it doesn't strike you as probable that Robinson Crusoe had any predisposition to lung trouble?
10037{_}3364{_}So you see, Dick True, as it is a poor doctor who is afraid of his own medicine, I am going to prescribe it first of all for ourselves, and we will go where unadulterated oxygen may be had for the smelling, and we can draw in sunshine with every breath."
10037{_}3365{_}The pale face brightened.
10037{_}3366{_}"Oh, that will be lovely!
10037{_}3367{_}I do get so tired of these old streets.
10037{_}3368{_}But John,--"  "Well, Dick?"
10037{_}3369{_}"Why do you keep calling me Dick True all the time?"
10037{_}3370{_}John laughed.
10037{_}3371{_}"Just to remind you that you must be a true boy before you can really be a True-man, Dick.
10037{_}3372{_}I want you to be in the best company.
10037{_}3373{_}Jesus Christ is the truth, you know, Dick."
10037{_}3374{_}"Jesus Christ," repeated the boy thoughtfully.
10037{_}3375{_}"I wish I knew him, John, as well as you do."
10037{_}3376{_}"If you love, you will know," said John, the light which the boy loved to watch creeping into his eyes.
10037{_}3377{_}"He is the best friend we will ever have, Dick, you and I."
10037{_}3378{_}He opened several papers as he spoke and ran his eyes over the advertising columns.
10037{_}3379{_}"H'm, I don't like the sound of these," he said, "they promise too much.
10037{_}3380{_}Hot and cold water baths and gas and the advantages of a private family and city privileges.
10037{_}3381{_}Everyone seems to keep the 'best table in the city.'
10037{_}3382{_}That's curious, isn't it, Dick?
10037{_}3383{_}And nearly everyone has the most convenient location.
10037{_}3384{_}Dick, my boy, it's one thing to say we are going to do a thing, it's another thing to do it.
10037{_}3385{_}I expect this suburban question is going to be a puzzle to you and me."
10037{_}3386{_}And so it proved.
10037{_}3387{_}Day after day John searched the papers in vain, until it seemed as if a suburban residence was the one thing in life unattainable.
10037{_}3388{_}But the long lane of disappointment had its turning at length, and he hurried home to Dick, paper in hand.
10037{_}3389{_}"Dick, Dick True, we've found it at last!
10037{_}3390{_}Listen:  "Two gentlemen can be pleasantly accommodated at 'The Willows.'
10037{_}3391{_}Address Miss Chillingworth, University P.O.
10037{_}3392{_}Box 123.
10037{_}3393{_}"The University Post Office is just near the College, you know, Dick, so it is in a good location.
10037{_}3394{_}Two gentlemen--that means you and me, Dick; and 'The Willows' means running brooks, or ought to, if they are any sort of respectable trees."
10037{_}3395{_}The boy clapped his hands.
10037{_}3396{_}"When can we go, John?"
10037{_}3397{_}John laughed.
10037{_}3398{_}"Not so fast, Dick.
10037{_}3399{_}There may be other gentlemen in Marlborough on the lookout for a suburban residence.
10037{_}3400{_}I addressed Miss Chillingworth on paper this morning, telling her I should give myself the pleasure of addressing her in person to-morrow.
10037{_}3401{_}It is a half holiday, you know, Dick.
10037{_}3402{_}I like the ring of this advertisement.
10037{_}3403{_}There is no fuss and feathers about it.
10037{_}3404{_}She doesn't offer city privileges and promise ice cream with every meal."
10037{_}3405{_}"But, John," said the boy, ruefully, "we're not gentlemen.
10037{_}3406{_}You don't wear a silk hat, you know, and I have no white shirts--nothing but these paper fronts.
10037{_}3407{_}I hate paper fronts!
10037{_}3408{_}They're such shams!
10037{_}3409{_}"Oh, ho!
10037{_}3410{_}Dick, so you're pining for frills, eh?
10037{_}3411{_}Well, if it will make you feel more comfortable, we'll go down to Stewart's and get fitted out to your satisfaction.
10037{_}3412{_}But don't forget that you can be a gentleman in homespun as well as broadcloth, Dick.
10037{_}3413{_}Real diamonds don't need to borrow any luster from their setting; only the paste do that."
10037{_}3414{_}The next afternoon John strode along in the direction of 'The Willows' to the accompaniment of a merry whistle.
10037{_}3415{_}It did him good to get out into the open country once more, and he felt sure it would be worth a king's ransom to Dick; but when he came in sight of the house he hesitated.
10037{_}3416{_}There must be some mistake.
10037{_}3417{_}This was not the sort of house to open its doors to boarders.
10037{_}3418{_}"Poor Dick!"
10037{_}3419{_}he soliloquized, "no wonder you felt a premonitory sense of the fitness of frills!
10037{_}3420{_}Well, I'll go and inquire.
10037{_}3421{_}They can only say 'No,' and that won't annihilate me."
10037{_}3422{_}He was ushered into Miss Diana's presence, and on the instant forgot everything but Miss Diana herself.
10037{_}3423{_}Before he realized what he was doing he had explained the reason of his seeking a suburban home, and, drawn on by her gentle sympathy, was telling her the story of his life.
10037{_}3424{_}Miss Diana had a way of compelling confidence, and the people who gave it to her never afterwards regretted the gift.
10037{_}3425{_}With the straightforwardness which was a part of his nature he told his story.
10037{_}3426{_}It never occurred to him that there was anything peculiar about it, yet when he had finished there were tears in his listener's eyes.
10037{_}3427{_}When at length he rose to go, everything was settled between them.
10037{_}3428{_}John's eyes wandered round the room and then rested again with a curious sense of pleasure upon Miss Diana's face.
10037{_}3429{_}"I cannot begin to thank you," he said, gratefully, "for allowing us to come here.
10037{_}3430{_}I never dared to hope that my poor little Dick would have such an education as this home will be to him, but I feel sure you will learn to like Dick True."
10037{_}3431{_}Miss Diana held out her hand, with a smile.
10037{_}3432{_}"I think I shall like you as well as Dick," she said.
10037{_}3433{_}*       *       *       *       *  Weeks and months flew past and the household at 'The Willows' was a very happy one.
10037{_}3434{_}Unavella was in great glee over the success of her scheme.
10037{_}3435{_}"I used ter think," she confided to her bosom friend, "thet boarders wuz good fer nuthin' 'cept ter be an aggervation an' a plague; but I couldn't think o' nuthin' else ter do, an' I made up my mind I'd ruther put up with 'em than lose Miss Di-an, even ef their antics did make me gray-headed afore the year wuz out.
10037{_}3436{_}But I needn't hev worritted.
10037{_}3437{_}Two sech obligin' young fellers I never did see, an' never expect ter agin in this world.
10037{_}3438{_}They don't never seem comfortable 'cept when they're helpin' a body.
10037{_}3439{_}An' Mr. John's whistle ez enuff ter put sunshine inter the Deluge!
10037{_}3440{_}I used ter think we wuz ez happy ez birds--Miss Di-an an' me--but I declare the house seems lonesum now when he leaves in the mornin'.
10037{_}3441{_}He's alluz at it, whistle, whistle, whistle.
10037{_}3442{_}'Tain't none o' them screechin' whistles that takes the top off of your head an' leaves the inside a' hummin', but it's jest as soft an' sweet an' low!
10037{_}3443{_}Sometimes I think he's prayin', it's that lovely.
10037{_}3444{_}It's my belief it puts Miss Di-an in mind o' someone, fer she jest sets in the porch, when he's a' tinkerin' round in the evenings or dig-gin' in the gardin--he's never satisfied unless everything's jest kep spick an' span--an' there's the sweetest smile on her face, an' the dreamy look in her eyes thet folks' eyes don't never hev 'cept when they're episodin' with their past.
10037{_}3445{_}"An' the way they foller her about an' treat her jest ez ef she wuz a princess!
10037{_}3446{_}I declare, it makes my heart warm.
10037{_}3447{_}The young one called her his little mother the other night, an' Mr. John sez, sez he, 'Ye couldn't hev a sweeter, Dick, nor a dearer.'
10037{_}3448{_}He makes me think of one o' them folks in poetry what wuz alluz a' ridin' round with banners an' a spear."
10037{_}3449{_}"A knight?"
10037{_}3450{_}suggested her friend, who had just indulged a literary taste by purchasing a paper covered edition of Sir Walter Scott.
10037{_}3451{_}"Yes, that's what I mean.
10037{_}3452{_}An' I sez to myself,--'ef they wuz like he is, an' wuz ez plenty in the Middle Ages ez they make 'em out ter be, then it's a pity we wuzn't back right in the center uv 'em,' sez I."
10037{_}3453{_}"Lady Di!
10037{_}3454{_}Lady Di!"
10037{_}3455{_}and little Dick came hurrying into the library where Miss Diana was sitting in the gloaming.
10037{_}3456{_}"John wants you to come out and see if you like the new flowers he is planting.
10037{_}3457{_}He says I must be sure to put your shawl on, for the dew is falling."
10037{_}3458{_}Miss Diana's eyes grew misty as her little cavalier adjusted her wrap.
10037{_}3459{_}"Why do you give me that name, Dick?"
10037{_}3460{_}she asked.
10037{_}3461{_}Only one other had ever given it to her before, in the long ago.
10037{_}3462{_}"What?
10037{_}3463{_}Lady Di?"
10037{_}3464{_}answered the boy.
10037{_}3465{_}"Oh, we always call you that, John and I.
10037{_}3466{_}Our Lady Di.
10037{_}3467{_}John says you make him think of the elect lady, in the Bible, you know."
10037{_}3468{_}And Miss Diana, as she passed the shelves, laid her hand caressingly upon the beloved books with a happy smile.
10037{_}3469{_}God had sent her the right ones!
10037{_}3470{_}CHAPTER XXII.
10037{_}3471{_}Marion entered Evadne's room one glorious winter's morning and threw herself on the lounge beside her cousin with a sigh.
10037{_}3472{_}"I don't see how you do it!"
10037{_}3473{_}she exclaimed.
10037{_}3474{_}"Do what?"
10037{_}3475{_}asked Evadne.
10037{_}3476{_}"Why, keep so pleasant with Isabelle.
10037{_}3477{_}She works me up to the last pitch of endurance, until I feel sometimes as if I should go wild.
10037{_}3478{_}It is no use saying anything, Mamma always takes her side, you know, but she does aggravate me so!
10037{_}3479{_}Even her movements irritate me,--just the way she shakes her head and curls her lip,--she is so self-satisfied.
10037{_}3480{_}She thinks no one else knows anything.
10037{_}3481{_}It must be a puzzle to her how the world ever got along before she came into it, and what it will do when she leaves it is a mystery!"
10037{_}3482{_}"She is good discipline."
10037{_}3483{_}Marion gave her an impetuous hug.
10037{_}3484{_}"You dear Evadne!
10037{_}3485{_}I believe you take us all as that!
10037{_}3486{_}But I don't think the rest of us can be quite as trying as Isabelle.
10037{_}3487{_}She does seem to delight in saying such horrid things.
10037{_}3488{_}She was abominably rude to you this morning at breakfast and yet you were just as polite as ever.
10037{_}3489{_}I couldn't have done it.
10037{_}3490{_}I should have sulked for a week.
10037{_}3491{_}I know you feel it, for I see your lips quiver--you are as susceptible to a rude touch as a sensitive plant--but it is beautiful to be able to keep sweet outside."
10037{_}3492{_}"You mean to be _kept_, Marion," said Evadne softly, "by the power of God.
10037{_}3493{_}I have no strength of my own."
10037{_}3494{_}Marion sighed dismally.
10037{_}3495{_}"Oh, dear!
10037{_}3496{_}I don't know what I mean, except that I'm a failure.
10037{_}3497{_}It is no wonder Louis thinks Christianity is a humbug, though he must confess there is something in it when he looks at you.
10037{_}3498{_}You are so different, Evadne!
10037{_}3499{_}I should think Isabelle would be ashamed of herself, for I believe half the time she says things on purpose to provoke you.
10037{_}3500{_}She doesn't seem to get much comfort out of it any way.
10037{_}3501{_}I never saw such a discontented mortal.
10037{_}3502{_}Don't you think it is wicked for people to grumble the way she does, Evadne?
10037{_}3503{_}It is growing on her, too.
10037{_}3504{_}She finds fault with everything.
10037{_}3505{_}Even the snow came in for a share of her disapprobation this morning, because it would spoil the skating, as if the Lord had no other plans to further than just to give her an afternoon's amusement!
10037{_}3506{_}She is _so_ self-centered!"
10037{_}3507{_}Evadne looked out at the street where the fresh fallen snow had spread a dazzling carpet of virgin white.
10037{_}3508{_}"He is going to let me give an afternoon's amusement to Gretchen and little Hans," she said.
10037{_}3509{_}"Uncle Lawrence has promised me the sleigh and I am going to take them to the Park.
10037{_}3510{_}Won't it be beautiful to see them enjoy!
10037{_}3511{_}Hans has never seen the trees after a snowstorm."
10037{_}3512{_}"That is you all over, Evadne.
10037{_}3513{_}It is always other people's pleasure, while I think of my own!
10037{_}3514{_}Oh, dear!
10037{_}3515{_}I seem to do nothing but get savage and then sigh over it.
10037{_}3516{_}I know it is dreadful to talk about my own sister as I have been doing--they say you ought to hide the faults of your relations--but it is only to you, you know.
10037{_}3517{_}Do you suppose there is any hope for me, Evadne?"
10037{_}3518{_}she asked disconsolately.
10037{_}3519{_}Evadne drew her head down until it was on a level with her own.
10037{_}3520{_}"Let Christ teach you to love, dear," she whispered, "Then, 'charity will cover the multitude of sins.'"
