10037{_}4459{_}"And some day you will forget me--men do such things they say--and another woman will be your wife and I will be all alone!"
10037{_}4460{_}"Sister!"
10037{_}4461{_}The abject man in the chair held out his hands in an agony of entreaty, "Come here and help us--if you can!"
10037{_}4462{_}and Evadne came swiftly into the room, and, sitting down on the side of the bed, gathered the pitiful little figure to her heart.
10037{_}4463{_}"It is not death but life," she said gently.
10037{_}4464{_}"This body is not _you_.
10037{_}4465{_}The home of the soul is more beautiful than, any earthly home can ever be.
10037{_}4466{_}It is those who are left behind dear, who mourn, not those who go."
10037{_}4467{_}Elise Hawthorne laid her head on Evadne's shoulder like a tired child.
10037{_}4468{_}"But I am afraid," she whispered.
10037{_}4469{_}"If this is true, and God is holy, I am not fit, you know."
10037{_}4470{_}"Your Father loves you dear, for he sent his Son to die.
10037{_}4471{_}The thief on the cross was a sinner, yet Christ took him to Paradise.
10037{_}4472{_}The fitness must come from Jesus.
10037{_}4473{_}His blood washes whiter than snow."
10037{_}4474{_}"But I have done nothing to earn it.
10037{_}4475{_}I have lived for myself alone."
10037{_}4476{_}"We never can earn a gift, dear.
10037{_}4477{_}God gives in a royal way.
10037{_}4478{_}He says to you only 'Believe I have given you life through my Son.'"
10037{_}4479{_}Evadne had taken the tiny Bible which she always carried from her pocket and was turning its pages rapidly.
10037{_}4480{_}"Here it is.
10037{_}4481{_}Will you raise the blind, Mr. Hawthorne, that your wife may see for herself?
10037{_}4482{_}'God so loved the world that he gave his only begotten Son,'--the best he had!--'that whosoever believeth in him should not perish,' you see there is no death for those who trust in him.
10037{_}4483{_}And then 'He that believeth on the Son _hath_ everlasting life.'
10037{_}4484{_}It does not mean that we may have it after years of toil.
10037{_}4485{_}The Israelites, stung by the serpents, had no time to reason or plan to live better, for they were dying, but they could turn their eyes to the brazen serpent which God had ordered to be lifted up in the midst of tho camp for an antidote to the poison.
10037{_}4486{_}So Christ has been 'lifted up' upon the cross for us.
10037{_}4487{_}He died instead of you.
10037{_}4488{_}Why should you die forever when he has paid your ransom and set you free?"
10037{_}4489{_}"But I cannot touch him,--I cannot be sure it is true."
10037{_}4490{_}"The Israelites could not touch the brazen serpent.
10037{_}4491{_}They simply looked, and lived.
10037{_}4492{_}There is just one condition for us to-day and it is 'Believe.'
10037{_}4493{_}Cannot you take your Heavenly Father at his word as you would your husband?
10037{_}4494{_}Cannot you treat God the same?"
10037{_}4495{_}Mrs. Hawthorne looked wonderingly at her nurse.
10037{_}4496{_}"Treat him the same as I do my husband!"
10037{_}4497{_}she exclaimed.
10037{_}4498{_}"Why, with Reginald, I believe every word he says."
10037{_}4499{_}"And I with God," said Evadne reverently.
10037{_}4500{_}"What charm have you wrought?"
10037{_}4501{_}asked John Randolph in a whisper, as they stood together that evening beside a quiet sleeper.
10037{_}4502{_}"This is the first natural sleep she has had.
10037{_}4503{_}I believe it will prove her salvation."
10037{_}4504{_}Evadne looked up at him, and over her face a light was breaking, "I have led her to Jesus, the Mighty to save."
10037{_}4505{_}*       *       *       *       *  The Hawthornes were going to Europe.
10037{_}4506{_}The young wife's convalescence had been tedious and it was a very frail little figure which clung to Evadne the evening before they started.
10037{_}4507{_}They had pleaded with her to go with them.
10037{_}4508{_}"Give up this toilsome work which is overtaxing your strength," Reginald had said, as they sat together one evening in the twilight, "and make your home with us.
10037{_}4509{_}You have grown to be our sister in the truest sense of the word and we have learned to lean upon you, Elise and I.
10037{_}4510{_}We can never hope to repay you," he continued huskily, "but it would be such a pleasure to have you with us for good."
10037{_}4511{_}Evadne looked at the pleading eyes with which Elise Hawthorne seconded her husband's wish and her lips trembled.
10037{_}4512{_}"How rich God is making me in friends!"
10037{_}4513{_}she said.
10037{_}4514{_}"I shall never forget that this thing has been in your hearts, but I must be about my Father's business."
10037{_}4515{_}And then John Randolph had come to make one of his pleasant, informal visits and they had sat together in a beautiful fellowship, talking of the things pertaining to the Kingdom.
10037{_}4516{_}"Doctor Randolph," Elise asked suddenly, "what is your conception of prayer?
10037{_}4517{_}Evadne says it means to her communion and companionship with Jesus.
10037{_}4518{_}She says it is 'the practice of the presence of God.'"
10037{_}4519{_}John Randolph's face grew luminous.
10037{_}4520{_}"To me it means a great stillness," he said.
10037{_}4521{_}"Did you ever think of the silences of God?
10037{_}4522{_}'Be still, and know that I am God,' 'Stand still, and see his salvation.'"
10037{_}4523{_}"But are we not to ask for what we want?"
10037{_}4524{_}asked Mrs. Hawthorne wonderingly.
10037{_}4525{_}"Oh, yes, but we learn to ask so little for ourselves when we love our Father's will.
10037{_}4526{_}The trouble is, we, want to do the talking.
10037{_}4527{_}God would have us listen while he speaks."
10037{_}4528{_}"Then what does it mean to worship God?"
10037{_}4529{_}she asked.
10037{_}4530{_}"We cannot always be in church."
10037{_}4531{_}John Randolph smiled.
10037{_}4532{_}"We do not need to be.
10037{_}4533{_}If our hearts are all on fire with the love of God, we worship him continually."
10037{_}4534{_}When he rose to go he turned towards Evadne.
10037{_}4535{_}"How goes life with you now, dear friend?"
10037{_}4536{_}The grey eyes, full of a clear shining, were lifted to his, "I am absolutely satisfied with Jesus Christ."
10037{_}4537{_}Marion was married and living in New York.
10037{_}4538{_}Louis had taken a small house, where he lived with his mother and Isabelle.
10037{_}4539{_}He spent his days in the monotonous routine of a hank, and to his pleasure-loving nature the drudgery seemed intolerable, but he said little.
10037{_}4540{_}Evadne never complained!
10037{_}4541{_}One day he went to see her at the Hospital and she was frightened at the pallor of his face.
10037{_}4542{_}She led him to the superintendent's reception room--there they would be undisturbed.
10037{_}4543{_}He staggered blindly as he entered the room and then sank heavily on a sofa near the door.
10037{_}4544{_}He looked like an old man.
10037{_}4545{_}"Louis!"
10037{_}4546{_}she cried in alarm, "what is the matter?"
10037{_}4547{_}He took a letter from his pocket and held it toward her.
10037{_}4548{_}It bore her own name, and the writing was her father's!
10037{_}4549{_}"Can you _ever_ forgive?"
10037{_}4550{_}Then he buried his face in his arms and groaned aloud.
10037{_}4551{_}The awful disgrace and shame of it seemed more than he could bear.
10037{_}4552{_}Interminable seemed the hours after Louis had left her, walking slowly, with that strange, grey shadow upon his face, and stooping as if some unseen burden were crushing him to the earth.
10037{_}4553{_}She dared not let herself think.
10037{_}4554{_}She must wait until she was alone.
10037{_}4555{_}At last she was free to go to her room.
10037{_}4556{_}Down on her knees she read the passionate farewell words, which made her heart thrill, so full of tender advice and loving thought for her comfort.
10037{_}4557{_}Through streaming tears she looked at the closely written pages of instructions, so minute that she could not err--and he had disliked writing so much!
10037{_}4558{_}This was the weary task which had tried him so!
10037{_}4559{_}And all these years she had never known.
10037{_}4560{_}She had been robbed of her birthright!
10037{_}4561{_}Fierce and long the battle raged.
10037{_}4562{_}When it was ended God heard his child cry softly, "Forgive us our trespasses as we forgive those who trespass against us."
10037{_}4563{_}She had forgiven!
10037{_}4564{_}CHAPTER XXXI.
10037{_}4565{_}Mrs. Simpson Kennard was sitting in her pretty morning room with her baby on her knee.
10037{_}4566{_}She looked across the room at her sister who was paying her a visit.
10037{_}4567{_}"I wish you had a little child to love, Isabelle.
10037{_}4568{_}It makes life so different.
10037{_}4569{_}I am just wrapped up in Florimel."
10037{_}4570{_}"For pity's sake, Marion," cried Isabelle peevishly, "don't you grow to be one of those tiresome women who think the whole world is interested in a baby's tooth!
10037{_}4571{_}I certainly do not echo your wish.
10037{_}4572{_}I think children are a nuisance."
10037{_}4573{_}Marion caught up her baby in dismay.
10037{_}4574{_}"Why, Isabelle, just think how much they do for us!
10037{_}4575{_}They broaden our sympathies--I read that only the other day, and----"  "Broaden your fiddlesticks!"
10037{_}4576{_}said Isabelle contemptuously.
10037{_}4577{_}"Easy for you to talk when you have everything you want!
10037{_}4578{_}If you had to live in that poky little house in Marlborough, I guess you would not find anything very broadening about them!
10037{_}4579{_}"It is perfectly preposterous to think of our being reduced to such a style of living!"
10037{_}4580{_}she continued, as Mrs. Kennard strove to soothe her baby's injured feelings with kisses.
10037{_}4581{_}"Just fancy, only one servant!
10037{_}4582{_}I never thought a Hildreth would fall so low."
10037{_}4583{_}"But you and Mamma are comfortable, Isabelle.
10037{_}4584{_}It is not as if you were forced to do anything."
10037{_}4585{_}"Do anything!"
10037{_}4586{_}echoed Isabelle.
10037{_}4587{_}"Are you going crazy?"
10037{_}4588{_}"Well, see how hard Evadne has to work?
10037{_}4589{_}and she is a Hildreth as well as you."
10037{_}4590{_}"Evadne!"
10037{_}4591{_}said Isabelle sarcastically, "with her nerves of steel and spine of adamant!
10037{_}4592{_}Evadne will never kill herself with work.
10037{_}4593{_}She is too much taken up with her wealthy private patients.
10037{_}4594{_}You should have seen her driving round with the Hawthornes in their elegant carriage And I reduced to dependence upon the electric cars!
10037{_}4595{_}I don't see how she manages to worm her way into people's confidence as she seems to do.
10037{_}4596{_}I couldn't, but then I have such a horror of being forward."
10037{_}4597{_}"'All doors are open to those who smile.'
10037{_}4598{_}I believe that is the reason, Isabelle."
10037{_}4599{_}"Stuff and nonsense!"
10037{_}4600{_}was Miss Hildreth's inelegant reply.
10037{_}4601{_}"She is a dear girl, Isabelle.
10037{_}4602{_}Why will you persist in disliking her so?"
10037{_}4603{_}"Oh, pray spare me any panegyrics!"
10037{_}4604{_}said Isabelle carelessly.
10037{_}4605{_}"It is bad enough to have Louis blazing up like a volcano if one has the temerity to mention her ladyship's name."
10037{_}4606{_}"How is Louis?"
10037{_}4607{_}asked Mrs. Kennard, finding she was treading on dangerous ground.
10037{_}4608{_}"Oh, the same as usual.
10037{_}4609{_}He looks like a ghost, and is about as cheerful as a cemetery.
10037{_}4610{_}He spends his holidays going over musty old letters in papa's desk.
10037{_}4611{_}I'm sure I don't see what fun he finds in it.
10037{_}4612{_}It is so selfish in him, when he might be giving mamma and me some pleasure--but Louis never did think of anyone but himself.
10037{_}4613{_}One day I found him stretched across the desk and it gave me such a fright!
10037{_}4614{_}You know what a state my nerves are in.
10037{_}4615{_}I thought he was in a fit or something,--he just looked like death, and he didn't seem to hear me when I called.
10037{_}4616{_}He had a large envelope addressed to papa in his hand and there was another under his arm that didn't look as if it had ever been opened, but I couldn't see the address.
10037{_}4617{_}I ran for mamma, but before we got back he was gone and the letters with him.
10037{_}4618{_}Whatever it was, it has had an awful effect upon him, though he won't give us any satisfaction, you know how provoking he is.
10037{_}4619{_}It is my belief he is going into decline, and I have such a horror of contagious diseases!
10037{_}4620{_}"If Evadne is so anxious to work, why doesn't she come and help mamma and me?
10037{_}4621{_}It is the least she could do after all we have done for her, but as mamma says, 'It is just a specimen of the ingratitude there is in the world.'"
10037{_}4622{_}*       *       *       *       *  The months rolled by and Evadne sat one afternoon in the superintendent's reception room reading a letter which the postman had just delivered.
10037{_}4623{_}It bore the Vernon postmark.
10037{_}4624{_}She had seen but little of Mrs. Everidge through the years which followed her graduation.
10037{_}4625{_}She had been constantly busy and her aunt's hands had been full, for her husband's health had failed utterly and he demanded continual care.
10037{_}4626{_}Now her long, beautiful ministry was over, for Horace Everidge, serenely selfish to the last, had fallen into the slumber which knows no earthly waking, and Aunt Marthe was free.
10037{_}4627{_}"I do not know what it means," she wrote, "but something tells me I shall not be long in Vernon.
10037{_}4628{_}I am just waiting to see what work the King has for me to do."
10037{_}4629{_}Evadne pressed the letter to her lips.
10037{_}4630{_}"Dear Aunt Marthe!
10037{_}4631{_}If the majority had had your 'tribulum' they would think they had earned the right to play!"
10037{_}4632{_}She looked up.
10037{_}4633{_}John Randolph was standing before her with a package in his hands.
10037{_}4634{_}"I have been commissioned by the Hawthornes to give this into your own possession," he said with a smile.
10037{_}4635{_}She opened it wonderingly.
10037{_}4636{_}Bonds and certificates of stock bearing her name.
10037{_}4637{_}What did it mean?
10037{_}4638{_}John Randolph had drawn a chair opposite her and was watching her face closely.
10037{_}4639{_}"You cannot think what long consultations we have held on the subject of what you would like," he said, "you seemed to have no wishes of your own.
10037{_}4640{_}At last a happy thought struck Reginald, and he sent me a power of attorney to make the transfer of these bonds and stocks to you.
10037{_}4641{_}It is a Trust Fund to be used to help souls.
10037{_}4642{_}We all thought that would please you best of all.
10037{_}4643{_}You are a rich woman, Miss Hildreth."
10037{_}4644{_}A great wave of joy swept over her bewildered face.
10037{_}4645{_}"So God has sent me the fulfilment of my dream!"
10037{_}4646{_}she said softly.
10037{_}4647{_}And John Randolph understood.
10037{_}4648{_}That evening she wrote to Mrs. Everidge.
10037{_}4649{_}"Dear Aunt Marthe,--The King's work is waiting for you in Marlborough.
10037{_}4650{_}The work that we used to long for--the joy of lifting the shadows from the hearts of the heavy laden--God has given to you and me!"
10037{_}4651{_}*       *       *       *       *  "Why should you not come to 'The Willows'?"
10037{_}4652{_}John Randolph put the question one afternoon, as they were enjoying Miss Diana's hospitality in the fragrant porch.
10037{_}4653{_}Evadne had just finished a merry recital of their woes.
10037{_}4654{_}"We have looked at houses until we are fairly distracted, Aunt Marthe and I.
10037{_}4655{_}One had a cellar kitchen, and I am not going to have my good Dyce buried in a cellar kitchen; and one had no bathroom, and another was all stairs; and they are all nothing but brick and mortar with a scrap of sky between.
10037{_}4656{_}I want trees and water and fields.
10037{_}4657{_}The poor souls have enough of masonry in their daily lives."
10037{_}4658{_}"I believe it is decreed that you should come here," he continued, after the first exclamations of surprise were over.
10037{_}4659{_}"It is just the work our lady delights in, and she cannot be left alone.
10037{_}4660{_}Dick goes to College next month and I must live in town.
10037{_}4661{_}The house is beautiful for situation, and a threefold cord of love and faith cannot easily be broken."
10037{_}4662{_}He looked round upon them, this man who found his joy in helping others, and waited for their answer.
10037{_}4663{_}"It would be beautiful, beautiful!"
10037{_}4664{_}cried Evadne, "if Miss Chillingworth were willing.
10037{_}4665{_}But the house is not large enough, Doctor Randolph, we shall need three or four guest chambers, you know."
10037{_}4666{_}"Nothing easier than to build an addition," said John, with the quiet reserve of power which always made his patients believe in the impossible.
10037{_}4667{_}Evadne laid her hand upon Miss Chillingworth's--"Dear Miss Diana," she said gently, "you do not say 'No' to us; do you think you could ever find it in your heart to say 'Yes'?
10037{_}4668{_}I know it must seem a terrible innovation, but we could never have imagined anything half so delightful, Aunt Marthe and I.
10037{_}4669{_}The atmosphere--outdoors and in--is perfection!"
10037{_}4670{_}Miss Diana looked at the sparkling face and then at Mrs. Everidge with her gentle smile.
10037{_}4671{_}"I find myself _very_ glad," she said, "since I have to lose my boys, but do you think we had better make any definite plans, dear, until we have talked it over with the Lord?"
10037{_}4672{_}And John Randolph said to Evadne with eyes that were suspiciously bright; "It is impossible for anyone to get very far from the Kingdom, when they live with our Lady Di."
10037{_}4673{_}The talk had wandered then to different subjects, and John Randolph listened to the soft play of Evadne's fancy and watched the light in her wonderful eyes.
10037{_}4674{_}Her nature, so long repressed in an uncongenial environment, in this new soil of love and sympathy was blossoming richly and he found her very fair.
10037{_}4675{_}He had rarely seen her resting.
10037{_}4676{_}Now the shapely hands were folded together in a beautiful stillness--and then the breeze had waved aside a flower, and a sunbeam, darting through the trellis, fell upon the stone in her ring and made it sparkle with a baleful fire!
10037{_}4677{_}"Poor Louis!"
10037{_}4678{_}Isabelle had said, the last time he had been called to prescribe for her frequently recurring attacks of indisposition, "he will have to wait for promotion now before he can think of marriage.
10037{_}4679{_}It is very hard for him."
10037{_}4680{_}So again the truth and the lie had mingled.
10037{_}4681{_}CHAPTER XXXII.
10037{_}4682{_}Very sweet grew the life at 'The Willows' and Mrs. Everidge and Evadne and Miss Diana found their hands full of happy work.
10037{_}4683{_}Unavella still reigned supreme in her kitchen.
10037{_}4684{_}"'Tain't a great sight harder to cook for a dozen than six," she had remarked sententiously, when the plan was unfolded to her, "it's only a matter uv quantity, the quality's jest the same.
10037{_}4685{_}Ef Miss Di-an's a'goin ter start in ter be a she Atlas an' carry the world on her shoulders, she'll find I'm warranted ter wash an' not shrink in the rinsin'.
10037{_}4686{_}I'm not a'goin ter be left behind, without I hev changed my name."
10037{_}4687{_}Dyce kept the rooms in spotless order and waited upon the guests.
10037{_}4688{_}"Dear friend," said Evadne one morning, as she watched her putting loving touches to the dining table, "you take as much trouble as if you expected Jesus Christ to be here!"
10037{_}4689{_}"So I does, Miss 'Vadney," she answered simply, "I never feels comfortable 'cept when dere's a place fer de Lord," and Evadne answered, "Dear Dyce, you make me feel ashamed!"
10037{_}4690{_}Many and varied were the guests who partook of their hospitality.
10037{_}4691{_}The famine which no material wealth can alleviate is not confined to the dwellings of the poor.
10037{_}4692{_}Hearts starve beneath coverings of velvet and loneliness often rides in a carriage.
10037{_}4693{_}Many were the patients whom the world counted "well to do" that John Randolph sent to Evadne to be comforted.
10037{_}4694{_}There was nothing to make them suspect that the keen intuition of the young physician had read their secret.
10037{_}4695{_}'The Willows' was simply a charming retreat where he sent them to try his favorite tonics of sunlight and oxygen; they never dreamed they were to be the recipients of favors which would not be rendered in the bill.
10037{_}4696{_}It was a beautiful fellowship in which they were banded together, for the Hawthornes had returned and were learning to find their pleasure in doing their Father's will.
10037{_}4697{_}Dick True was in the brotherhood also, and never came home for his vacations without bringing with him "some fellow who needed a taste of love," and the overgrown boys would glory in their strength as they lifted Miss Diana from the carriage after a delightful drive, and learn a strange gentleness as they were unconsciously trained in the little deeds of chivalry which bespeak a true man.
10037{_}4698{_}Soon after Evadne's dream had materialized John Randolph had sent her a dainty little equipage to help on the work.
10037{_}4699{_}"You are too kind!"
10037{_}4700{_}she cried, as she thanked him, "too generous!"
10037{_}4701{_}"Can we be that?"
10037{_}4702{_}he asked, "when we are giving to a King?
10037{_}4703{_}It is a theory of mine that a drive in the country with the right companion is better than exordiums.
10037{_}4704{_}These poor souls have never learned to see 'sermons in stones, books in the running brooks, and God in everything.'
10037{_}4705{_}You must give me the pleasure of a little share in your beautiful work, my friend."
10037{_}4706{_}"A little share!"
10037{_}4707{_}echoed Evadne.
10037{_}4708{_}"Is it possible that you do not know, Doctor Randolph, how much of it belongs to you!"
10037{_}4709{_}The beauty of the life was that the guests were taken into the heart of the living and felt themselves a part of the home.
10037{_}4710{_}They never preached, these wise, tender women, but the beautiful incidental teachings sank deep into hearts that would have been closed fast against sermons.
10037{_}4711{_}There was no stereotyped effort to do them good, they simply lived as Christ did, and the world-tired souls looked on and marveled, and rejoiced in the sunlight of the present and the afterglow which made the memory of their visit a delight.
10037{_}4712{_}"'Do not leave the sky out of your landscape,'" said Aunt Marthe in her cheery way, as Mrs. Dolours was wailing over her troubles.
10037{_}4713{_}That was all--for the time,--Mrs. Everidge believed in homeopathy--but it set her hearer thinking, and thought found expression in questioning, until she was led to the feet of the great Teacher and learned to roll her burden of trouble upon him who came to bear the burdens of the world.
10037{_}4714{_}"'We are not to be anxious about living but about living well,'" said Miss Diana to a young man who prided himself upon being a philosopher "that is a maxim of Plato's but we can only carry it out by the help of the Lord, my boy."
10037{_}4715{_}And he listened to Evadne's merry laugh as she pelted Hans with cherries while Gretchen dreamed of the Fatherland under the trees by the brook, and wondered whether after all the men who had made it their aim to stifle every natural inclination, had learned the true secret of living as well as these happy souls who laid their cares down at the feet of their Father, and gave their lives into Christ's keeping day by day.
10037{_}4716{_}"You just seem to live in the present," wealthy Mrs. Greyson said with a sigh, as she folded her jeweled fingers over her rich brocade, "I don't see how you do it!
10037{_}4717{_}Life is one long presentiment with me.
10037{_}4718{_}I am filled with such horrible forebodings.
10037{_}4719{_}I tell Doctor Randolph, it is a sort of moral nightmare."
10037{_}4720{_}"Some of your griefs you have cured,   And the sharpest you still have survived,   But what torments of pain you endured,   From evils that never arrived!"
10037{_}4721{_}Evadne quoted the words from a book of old French poems she had found in the library.
10037{_}4722{_}Then she asked gently, "Why should you worry about the future, dear Mrs. Greyson, when it is such a waste of time?
10037{_}4723{_}Don't you believe our Father loves his children?
10037{_}4724{_}"A waste of time."
10037{_}4725{_}That was a new way of looking at it!
10037{_}4726{_}Mrs. Greyson had always prided herself upon being thrifty, and, if God loved, would he let any real harm happen?
10037{_}4727{_}She knew she would shield her children.
10037{_}4728{_}How blind she had been!
10037{_}4729{_}"Ah, but you have never known sorrow!"
10037{_}4730{_}and Mrs. Morner drew her sable draperies around her with a sigh.
10037{_}4731{_}"Just look at your face!
10037{_}4732{_}Not a shadow upon it and hardly a wrinkle.
10037{_}4733{_}You are one of the favored ones with whom life has been all sunshine."
10037{_}4734{_}Mrs. Everidge laughed brightly.
10037{_}4735{_}She had never pined to pose as a martyr before the world.
10037{_}4736{_}"God has been wondrous kind to me," she said, "but there is a cure for all sorrow, dear friend, in his love.
10037{_}4737{_}The great Physician is the only one who has a medicament for that disease.
10037{_}4738{_}It is not forgetfulness, you know--he does not deal in narcotics--but he lays his pierced hand upon our bleeding hearts and stills their pain.
10037{_}4739{_}Our memory is as fresh as ever, but it is memory with the sting taken out."
10037{_}4740{_}"Ah, but you cannot understand--how should you?
10037{_}4741{_}You have always had everything you wanted, and you have never lost anything or longed for what has been denied you!"
10037{_}4742{_}and a toilworn woman, whose life seemed one long battle with disappointment, looked enviously at Miss Diana, over whose peaceful face life's twilight was falling in tender colors.
10037{_}4743{_}"Not quite everything I wanted, dear," said Miss Diana softly, "but I have come to know that God himself is sufficient for all our needs."
10037{_}4744{_}"Our dear Miss Diana has learned that 'we must sit in the sunshine if we would reflect the rainbow,'" said Aunt Marthe in her low tones.
10037{_}4745{_}"It is a good rule, 'for every look we take at self, to take ten looks at Jesus.'
10037{_}4746{_}She lives in the light of his smile."
10037{_}4747{_}Then through the open window they heard Evadne singing,    "Oh, the little birds sang east, and the little birds sang west,   And I smiled to think God's greatness flowed around our incompleteness,   Round our restlessness, his rest."
10037{_}4748{_}And the weary soul folded its tired wings, all wounded with vain beatings against the prison bars of circumstance, and was hushed into a great stillness against the heart of its Father.
10037{_}4749{_}*       *       *       *       *  John Randolph sought Evadne in the familiar porch which had grown to be to him the sweetest spot on earth.
10037{_}4750{_}"You are always busy," he said with a smile, as he lifted the garment she was making for the little waif who was to have her first taste of heaven at 'The Willows.'
10037{_}4751{_}Satan has no chance to find an occupation for you."
10037{_}4752{_}"But, oh, Doctor Randolph, what a drop in the bucket all our doing seems, when we think of the need of the world!"
10037{_}4753{_}"Yet without the drops the bucket would be empty, dear friend.
10037{_}4754{_}God never expects the impossible from us, you know.
10037{_}4755{_}I think Christ's highest commendation will always be, 'She hath done what she could.'
10037{_}4756{_}It is when we neglect the doing that he is wounded."
10037{_}4757{_}After a pause he spoke again.
10037{_}4758{_}"With your permission I am going to send you a new patient."
10037{_}4759{_}There was no trace of the struggle through which he had passed.
10037{_}4760{_}This brave soul had learned to do the right and leave the rest with God.
10037{_}4761{_}Evadne laughed.
10037{_}4762{_}"Still they come!
10037{_}4763{_}Is it man, woman or child.
10037{_}4764{_}Doctor Randolph?"
10037{_}4765{_}"Your cousin Louis."
10037{_}4766{_}His voice was very still.
10037{_}4767{_}"Poor Louis!
10037{_}4768{_}Is it more serious then?
10037{_}4769{_}He has been looking wretchedly for months."
10037{_}4770{_}John Randolph examined her face critically.
10037{_}4771{_}Could she call him "poor Louis" if she loved?
10037{_}4772{_}"His present trouble is nervous strain, aggravated by the unaccustomed confinement, and some mental excitement under which he is laboring.
10037{_}4773{_}He must have a long rest, with a complete change of environment.
10037{_}4774{_}If anyone can lift the cloud which seems to be hanging over him, I think it is you."
10037{_}4775{_}Evadne shook her head sadly.
10037{_}4776{_}"The only one who can help Louis is Jesus Christ," she said.
10037{_}4777{_}CHAPTER XXXIII.
10037{_}4778{_}Louis Hildreth lay upon a couch in the cool library the morning after his arrival at 'The Willows.'
10037{_}4779{_}Evadne had been shocked at the change in him since she had seen him last.
10037{_}4780{_}His eyes were sunken, while underneath purple shadows fell upon his pallid cheeks.
10037{_}4781{_}He touched Evadne's hand as she sat beside him.
10037{_}4782{_}It was his hand!
10037{_}4783{_}"What a splendid fellow Randolph is!"
10037{_}4784{_}he exclaimed suddenly.
10037{_}4785{_}"He is making himself felt in Marlborough, I tell you.
10037{_}4786{_}Strange, how some men forge their way to the front, while the rest of us just float down the stream of mediocrity.
10037{_}4787{_}No wonder we are not missed, when we drop out of the babbling conglomerate of humanity into silence," he added bitterly.
10037{_}4788{_}"Who would miss a single pair of fins from amidst a shoal of herring!"
10037{_}4789{_}"I think it is because Doctor Randolph is not content to float, Louis," Evadne answered gently.
10037{_}4790{_}"He must always be climbing higher.
10037{_}4791{_}Like Paul, he is 'pressing towards the mark.'"
10037{_}4792{_}"He is a grand fellow!
10037{_}4793{_}And the beauty of it is he never seems to think of himself at all.
10037{_}4794{_}Most men would get to be top-lofty if they accomplished as much as he does every day."
10037{_}4795{_}Evadne's lips parted in a happy smile.
10037{_}4796{_}"I think Doctor Randolph is too much occupied with Jesus to have time to waste upon himself."
10037{_}4797{_}"Upon my word, coz, you're a puzzle!
10037{_}4798{_}You talk in an unknown tongue.
10037{_}4799{_}Don't you know Self is the god we worship, and the aim of our existence is to have it wear purple and fine linen, and fare sumptuously every day?"
10037{_}4800{_}"It should not be!"
10037{_}4801{_}cried Evadne.
10037{_}4802{_}"Oh Louis, dear Louis, life can never be grand until we are able to say--'Self has been crucified with Christ!'"
10037{_}4803{_}*       *       *       *       *  Weeks rolled into months and Louis was still at 'The Willows.'
10037{_}4804{_}His cynicism had come to have a strangely wistful ring.
10037{_}4805{_}John Randolph's visits were frequent and they held long conversations together, these men, the one who had seized every opportunity and made the most of it, the other who had let his golden chances slip through his fingers one by one; then John Randolph would go bravely back to his life of toil, while Louis listened to Evadne's sweet voice as she sang in the gloaming, or watched his ring glisten as her deft fingers were busy with their deeds of love.
10037{_}4806{_}"How do you do it?"
10037{_}4807{_}he exclaimed one evening when they were alone together.
10037{_}4808{_}"You never rest!
10037{_}4809{_}Your whole life seems to be centered in the lives of others, and there is nothing attractive about them, if there were I could understand.
10037{_}4810{_}It looks like such drudgery to me.
10037{_}4811{_}Tell me, little coz, what makes you give up all your ease to make these people happy?"
10037{_}4812{_}"When we love our Father it is our joy to do his will," she answered softly.
10037{_}4813{_}"If I could live like you and Randolph I should be perfectly satisfied.
10037{_}4814{_}I wish I had the courage to try."
10037{_}4815{_}"Mere outward living cannot save us, Louis.
10037{_}4816{_}Nothing can but faith in the atoning blood and the name and the love of Christ.
10037{_}4817{_}Then--when we believe, you know--all things become possible.
10037{_}4818{_}We make an awful mistake when we think we know better than the Bible.
10037{_}4819{_}Nicodemus lived a perfect outward life, yet Christ said to him, 'Except ye be born again--of the Word and the Spirit--ye cannot see the Kingdom of God.'
10037{_}4820{_}We are running a terrible risk when we try to live without Jesus."
10037{_}4821{_}"That is what Randolph says.
10037{_}4822{_}He is a one idea man, if ever there was one, and yet he is so many sided!
10037{_}4823{_}He is the most uncompromising fellow I ever knew.
10037{_}4824{_}I should as soon expect to see the stars fall from the sky as to see him do a shady thing.
10037{_}4825{_}You would be amused, coz, to see the lady mother and Isabelle joining forces to lay siege to his affections."
10037{_}4826{_}What meant that sudden start and then the blush which flamed up over cheek and brow?
10037{_}4827{_}Louis Hildreth closed his thin fingers over Evadne's ring with a long drawn sigh.
10037{_}4828{_}He was beginning to realize that a hand, without a heart, is an empty thing.
10037{_}4829{_}Long after she had left him he lay motionless.
10037{_}4830{_}This knowledge which had come to him so suddenly had a bitter taste.
10037{_}4831{_}*       *       *       *       *  "You ought to get well, Hildreth, and you ought to be a very happy man," John Randolph spoke the words suddenly as he rose to take his leave.
10037{_}4832{_}"I never expect to be either.
10037{_}4833{_}When a man has all he has prided himself upon swept away from him, and all that he longs for denied him, how can it be possible?"
10037{_}4834{_}"'Count it your highest good when God denies you.'
10037{_}4835{_}Is that too hard a gospel?
10037{_}4836{_}We shall not read it so in the light of eternity.
10037{_}4837{_}It is only that Christ may become to us the 'altogether lovely' One."
10037{_}4838{_}"Did you ever love--a woman?"
10037{_}4839{_}Louis put the question suddenly, watching his friend's face with a jealous scrutiny.
10037{_}4840{_}"Yes."
10037{_}4841{_}The answer was as simple and straightforward as the man.
10037{_}4842{_}He knew of nothing to be ashamed of in this beautiful love of his life.
10037{_}4843{_}"And her name was?--"  "Evadne."
10037{_}4844{_}John Randolph spoke the name for the first time to another, looking up at the sky.
10037{_}4845{_}When he turned to leave the room he saw that Louis' face was buried among his cushions and he drove away in a great wonderment.
10037{_}4846{_}What could it all mean?
10037{_}4847{_}"Knocking, knocking, who is there?
10037{_}4848{_}Waiting, waiting, oh, how fair!
10037{_}4849{_}'T is a pilgrim, strange and kingly,     Never such was seen before.
10037{_}4850{_}Ah, my soul, for such a wonder,     Wilt thou not undo the door?"
10037{_}4851{_}Evadne sang the words softly in the twilight: sang them with a great note of longing in her pleading voice.
10037{_}4852{_}She and her cousin were alone.
10037{_}4853{_}"Evadne, come here."
10037{_}4854{_}She crossed the room and knelt beside his couch.
10037{_}4855{_}"Little coz, I have let the Pilgrim in."
10037{_}4856{_}And Evadne buried her face in the cushions with a low cry.
10037{_}4857{_}The crown of rejoicing was hers--at last!
10037{_}4858{_}*       *       *       *       *  "There is only one thing wanting between you two."
10037{_}4859{_}Louis looked wistfully at John Randolph and Evadne, as they stood beside him, talking brightly of how he should help when he grew strong.
10037{_}4860{_}"And what is that?"
10037{_}4861{_}Doctor Randolph asked the question with a smile.
10037{_}4862{_}Louis drew his ring from Evadne's finger and laid her hand in that of his friend.
10037{_}4863{_}"Take her, Randolph, she is worthy of you.
10037{_}4864{_}I would not say that of any other woman."
10037{_}4865{_}With a great joy surging in his heart, John Randolph held out his other hand.
10037{_}4866{_}She must give herself.
10037{_}4867{_}He could not take her from another's giving.
10037{_}4868{_}A lovely shyness flushed into the pure face, their eyes met, and Evadne laid her hand in his without a word.
10037{_}4869{_}"Evadne!"
10037{_}4870{_}The rich, tender tones fell throbbing through the silence, enwrapping the name in a sweet protectiveness.
10037{_}4871{_}"Life is--for us--to do the will of God!"
10037{_}4872{_}THE END.
